desk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shoe-banging_incident "Shoe-banging incident") to interrupt a speech by Filipino delegate [Lorenzo Sumulong](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorenzo_Sumulong "Lorenzo Sumulong"), which set the general tone for the debates and speeches.<sup id="cite_ref-Gaddis_1997_182_170-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Gaddis_1997_182-170">[170]</a></sup> Castro delivered the longest speech ever held before the United Nations General Assembly, speaking for four and a half hours in a speech mostly given over to denouncing American policies towards Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-172"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Subsequently, visited by Polish first secretary [Władysław Gomułka](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Gomu%C5%82ka "Władysław Gomułka"), Bulgarian first secretary [Todor Zhivkov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Todor_Zhivkov "Todor Zhivkov"), Egyptian president [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser"), and Indian premier [Jawaharlal Nehru](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru "Jawaharlal Nehru"),<sup id="cite_ref-174"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Castro also received an evening's reception from the [Fair Play for Cuba Committee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_Play_for_Cuba_Committee "Fair Play for Cuba Committee").<sup id="cite_ref-175"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>

Back in Cuba, Castro feared a US-backed coup; in 1959 his regime spent $120 million on Soviet, French, and Belgian weaponry and by early 1960 had doubled the size of Cuba's armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-176"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Fearing counter-revolutionary elements in the army, the government created a People's Militia to arm citizens favourable to the revolution, training at least 50,000 civilians in combat techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-177"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> In September 1960, they created the [Committees for the Defense of the Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committees_for_the_Defense_of_the_Revolution "Committees for the Defense of the Revolution") (CDR), a nationwide civilian organization which implemented neighbourhood spying to detect counter-revolutionary activities as well as organizing health and education campaigns, becoming a conduit for public complaints. By 1970, a third of the population would be involved in the CDR, and this would eventually rise to 80%.<sup id="cite_ref-178"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Castro_and_Nasser.jpg)

Castro giving press statement next to Egypt's President [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser") before their meeting on the sidelines of United Nations General Assembly in 1960

Despite the fear of a coup, Castro garnered support in New York City. On 18 February 1961, 400 people—mainly Cubans, Puerto Ricans, and college students—picketed in the rain outside of the United Nations rallying for Castro's anti-colonial values and his effort to reduce the United States' power over Cuba. The protesters held up signs that read, "Mr. Kennedy, Cuba is Not For Sale.", "[Viva](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vive,_viva,_and_vivat "Vive, viva, and vivat") Fidel Castro!" and "Down With Yankee Imperialism!". Around 200 policemen were on the scene, but the protesters continued to chant slogans and throw pennies in support of Fidel Castro's socialist movement. Some Americans disagreed with President [John F. Kennedy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy "John F. Kennedy")'s decision to ban trade with Cuba, and outwardly supported his nationalist revolutionary tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-179"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>

Castro proclaimed the new administration a [direct democracy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_democracy "Direct democracy"), in which Cubans could assemble at demonstrations to express their democratic will. As a result, he rejected the need for elections, claiming that [representative democratic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Representative_democracy "Representative democracy") systems served the interests of socio-economic elites.<sup id="cite_ref-180"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> US Secretary of State [Christian Herter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Herter "Christian Herter") announced that Cuba was adopting the Soviet model of rule, with a one-party state, government control of trade unions, suppression of civil liberties, and the absence of freedom of speech and press.<sup id="cite_ref-181"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>

### Bay of Pigs Invasion and "Socialist Cuba": 1961–1962

> There was ... no doubt about who the victors were. Cuba's stature in the world soared to new heights, and Fidel's role as the adored and revered leader among ordinary Cuban people received a renewed boost. His popularity was greater than ever. In his own mind he had done what generations of Cubans had only fantasized about: he had taken on the United States and won.

– [Peter Bourne](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Bourne "Peter Bourne"), Castro biographer, 1986<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986226_182-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986226-182">[182]</a></sup>

In January 1961, Castro ordered [Havana's US Embassy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_States,_Havana "Embassy of the United States, Havana") to reduce its 300-member staff, suspecting that many of them were spies. The US responded by ending diplomatic relations, and it increased CIA funding for exiled dissidents; these militants began attacking ships that traded with Cuba, and bombed factories, shops, and sugar mills.<sup id="cite_ref-183"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Both President Eisenhower and his successor President Kennedy supported a CIA plan to aid a dissident militia, the Democratic Revolutionary Front, to invade Cuba and overthrow Castro; the plan resulted in the [Bay of Pigs Invasion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion "Bay of Pigs Invasion") in April 1961. On 15 April, CIA-supplied [B-26s](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Douglas_A-26_Invader "Douglas A-26 Invader") bombed three Cuban military airfields; the US announced that the perpetrators were defecting Cuban air force pilots, but Castro exposed these claims as [false flag](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_flag "False flag") misinformation.<sup id="cite_ref-184"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Fearing invasion, he ordered the arrest of between 20,000 and 100,000 suspected counter-revolutionaries,<sup id="cite_ref-185"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> publicly proclaiming, "What the imperialists cannot forgive us, is that we have made a Socialist revolution under their noses", his first announcement that the government was socialist.<sup id="cite_ref-186"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg)

[Che Guevara](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara "Che Guevara") (left) and Castro, photographed by [Alberto Korda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alberto_Korda "Alberto Korda") in 1961

The CIA and the Democratic Revolutionary Front had based a 1,400-strong army, Brigade 2506, in [Nicaragua](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicaragua "Nicaragua"). On the night of 16 to 17 April, Brigade 2506 landed along Cuba's [Bay of Pigs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs "Bay of Pigs") and engaged in a firefight with a local revolutionary militia. Castro ordered Captain José Ramón Fernández to launch the counter-offensive, before taking personal control of it. After bombing the invaders' ships and bringing in reinforcements, Castro forced the Brigade to surrender on 20 April.<sup id="cite_ref-187"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> He ordered the 1189 captured rebels to be interrogated by a panel of journalists on live television, personally taking over the questioning on 25 April. Fourteen were put on trial for crimes allegedly committed before the revolution, while the others were returned to the US in exchange for medicine and food valued at US$25 million.<sup id="cite_ref-188"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Castro's victory reverberated around the world, especially in Latin America, but it also increased internal opposition primarily among the middle-class Cubans who had been detained in the run-up to the invasion. Although most were freed within a few days, many fled to the US, establishing themselves in Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-189"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup>

Consolidating "Socialist Cuba", Castro united the MR-26-7, PSP and Revolutionary Directorate into a governing party based on the Leninist principle of [democratic centralism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_centralism "Democratic centralism"): the [Integrated Revolutionary Organizations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba "Communist Party of Cuba") (_Organizaciones Revolucionarias Integradas_ – ORI), renamed the United Party of the Cuban Socialist Revolution (PURSC) in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-190"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Although the USSR was hesitant regarding Castro's embrace of socialism,<sup id="cite_ref-191"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> relations with the Soviets deepened. Castro sent Fidelito for a Moscow schooling,<sup id="cite_ref-Bourne_1986_231_192-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Bourne_1986_231-192">[192]</a></sup> Soviet technicians arrived on the island,<sup id="cite_ref-Bourne_1986_231_192-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Bourne_1986_231-192">[192]</a></sup> and Castro was awarded the [Lenin Peace Prize](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenin_Peace_Prize "Lenin Peace Prize").<sup id="cite_ref-193"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> In December 1961, Castro admitted that he had been a Marxist–Leninist for years, and in his Second Declaration of Havana he called on Latin America to rise up in revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986230–234Geyer1991274Quirk1993395,_400–401Coltman2003190_194-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986230%E2%80%93234Geyer1991274Quirk1993395,_400%E2%80%93401Coltman2003190-194">[194]</a></sup> In response, the US successfully pushed the Organization of American States to expel Cuba; the Soviets privately reprimanded Castro for recklessness, although he received praise from China.<sup id="cite_ref-195"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> Despite their ideological affinity with China, in the [Sino-Soviet split](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split "Sino-Soviet split"), Cuba allied with the wealthier Soviets, who offered economic and military aid.<sup id="cite_ref-196"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup>

The ORI began shaping Cuba using the Soviet model, persecuting political opponents and perceived [social deviants](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deviance_(sociology) "Deviance (sociology)") such as prostitutes and homosexuals; Castro considered same-sex sexual activity a bourgeois trait.<sup id="cite_ref-197"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Gay men were forced into the [Military Units to Aid Production](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_Units_to_Aid_Production "Military Units to Aid Production") (_Unidades Militares de Ayuda a la Producción_ – UMAP); after many revolutionary intellectuals decried this move, the UMAP camps were closed in 1967, although gay men continued to be imprisoned.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993525–526Coltman2003188–189_198-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993525%E2%80%93526Coltman2003188%E2%80%93189-198">[198]</a></sup> By 1962, Cuba's economy was in steep decline, a result of poor economic management and low productivity coupled with the US trade embargo. Food shortages led to rationing, resulting in protests in [Cárdenas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%A1rdenas,_Cuba "Cárdenas, Cuba").<sup id="cite_ref-199"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> Security reports indicated that many Cubans associated austerity with the "Old Communists" of the PSP, while Castro considered a number of them—namely [Aníbal Escalante](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anibal_Escalante "Anibal Escalante") and [Blas Roca](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blas_Roca "Blas Roca")—unduly loyal to Moscow. In March 1962 Castro removed the most prominent "Old Communists" from office, labelling them "sectarian".<sup id="cite_ref-200"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> On a personal level, Castro was increasingly lonely, and his relations with Guevara became strained as the latter became increasingly anti-Soviet and pro-Chinese.<sup id="cite_ref-201"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup>

### Cuban Missile Crisis and furthering socialism: 1962–1968

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:U2_Image_of_Cuban_Missile_Crisis.jpg)

U-2 reconnaissance photograph of Soviet nuclear missiles in Cuba

Militarily weaker than [NATO](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO"), Khrushchev wanted to install Soviet [R-12](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/R-12_(missile) "R-12 (missile)") [MRBM](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/MRBM "MRBM") nuclear missiles on Cuba to even the power balance.<sup id="cite_ref-202"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> Although conflicted, Castro agreed, believing it would guarantee Cuba's safety and enhance the cause of socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-203"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> Undertaken in secrecy, only the Castro brothers, Guevara, Dorticós and security chief [Ramiro Valdés](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramiro_Vald%C3%A9s "Ramiro Valdés") knew the full plan.<sup id="cite_ref-204"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> Upon discovering it through aerial reconnaissance, in October the US implemented an island-wide [quarantine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quarantine "Quarantine") to search vessels headed to Cuba, sparking the [Cuban Missile Crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis "Cuban Missile Crisis"). The US saw the missiles as offensive; Castro insisted they were for defence only.<sup id="cite_ref-205"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> Castro urged that Khrushchev should launch a nuclear strike on the US if Cuba were invaded, but Khrushchev was desperate to avoid [nuclear war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_war "Nuclear war").<sup id="cite_ref-206"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Castro was left out of the negotiations, in which Khrushchev agreed to remove the missiles in exchange for a US commitment not to invade Cuba and an understanding that the US would remove their [MRBMs from Turkey and Italy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/PGM-19_Jupiter#Operational_deployment "PGM-19 Jupiter").<sup id="cite_ref-208"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Feeling betrayed by Khrushchev, Castro was furious and soon fell ill.<sup id="cite_ref-209"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Proposing a five-point plan, Castro demanded that the US end its embargo, withdraw from [Guantanamo Bay Naval Base](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_Naval_Base "Guantanamo Bay Naval Base"), cease supporting dissidents, and stop violating Cuban air space and territorial waters. He presented these demands to [U Thant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/U_Thant "U Thant"), visiting [Secretary-General of the United Nations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations "Secretary-General of the United Nations"), but the US ignored them. In turn Castro refused to allow the UN's inspection team into Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-210"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup>

In May 1963, Castro visited the USSR at Khrushchev's personal invitation, touring 14 cities, addressing a [Red Square](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Square "Red Square") rally, and being awarded both the [Order of Lenin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Lenin "Order of Lenin") and an honorary doctorate from [Moscow State University](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow_State_University "Moscow State University").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986245–248Quirk1993458–470Coltman2003204–205_211-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986245%E2%80%93248Quirk1993458%E2%80%93470Coltman2003204%E2%80%93205-211">[211]</a></sup> Castro returned to Cuba with new ideas; inspired by Soviet newspaper _[Pravda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pravda "Pravda")_, he amalgamated _Hoy_ and _Revolución_ into a new daily, _[Granma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Granma_(newspaper) "Granma (newspaper)")_,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986249Quirk1993538_212-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986249Quirk1993538-212">[212]</a></sup> and oversaw large investment into Cuban sport that resulted in an increased international sporting reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986249–250Quirk1993702_213-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986249%E2%80%93250Quirk1993702-213">[213]</a></sup> Seeking to further consolidate control, in 1963 the government cracked down on Protestant sects in Cuba, with Castro labelling them counter-revolutionary "instruments of imperialism"; many preachers were found guilty of illegal US links and imprisoned.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993435–434_214-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993435%E2%80%93434-214">[214]</a></sup> Measures were implemented to force perceived idle and delinquent youths to work, primarily through the introduction of mandatory military service.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993454–454,_479–480_215-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993454%E2%80%93454,_479%E2%80%93480-215">[215]</a></sup> In September, the government temporarily permitted emigration for anyone other than males aged between 15 and 26, thereby ridding the government of thousands of critics, most of whom were from upper and middle-class backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993530–534Coltman2003213_216-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993530%E2%80%93534Coltman2003213-216">[216]</a></sup> In 1963, Castro's mother died. This was the last time his private life was reported in Cuba's press.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986250–251_217-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986250%E2%80%93251-217">[217]</a></sup> In January 1964, Castro returned to Moscow, officially to sign a new five-year sugar trade agreement, but also to discuss the ramifications of the [assassination of John F. Kennedy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy "Assassination of John F. Kennedy").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986263Quirk1993488–489_218-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986263Quirk1993488%E2%80%93489-218">[218]</a></sup> Castro was deeply concerned by the assassination, believing that a far-right conspiracy was behind it but that the Cubans would be blamed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993484–486_219-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993484%E2%80%93486-219">[219]</a></sup> In October 1965, the Integrated Revolutionary Organizations was officially renamed the "Cuban Communist Party" and published the membership of its Central Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993534Coltman2003213_220-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993534Coltman2003213-220">[220]</a></sup>

> The greatest threat presented by Castro's Cuba is as an example to other Latin American states which are beset by poverty, corruption, feudalism, and plutocratic exploitation ... his influence in Latin America might be overwhelming and irresistible if, with Soviet help, he could establish in Cuba a Communist utopia.

– [Walter Lippmann](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Lippmann "Walter Lippmann"), _[Newsweek](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newsweek "Newsweek")_, 27 April 1964<sup id="cite_ref-221"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup>

Despite Soviet misgivings, Castro continued to call for global revolution, funding militant leftists and those engaged in [national liberation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_liberation "National liberation") struggles. Cuba's foreign policy was strongly anti-imperialist, believing that every nation should control its own natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993744_222-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993744-222">[222]</a></sup> He supported Che Guevara's "Andean project", an unsuccessful plan to set up a guerrilla movement in the highlands of [Bolivia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolivia "Bolivia"), [Peru](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peru "Peru") and [Argentina](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina "Argentina"). He allowed revolutionary groups from around the world, from the [Viet Cong](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viet_Cong "Viet Cong") to the [Black Panthers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Panther_Party "Black Panther Party"), to train in Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986255Coltman2003211_223-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986255Coltman2003211-223">[223]</a></sup> He considered Western-dominated Africa to be ripe for revolution and sent troops and medics to aid [Ahmed Ben Bella](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Ben_Bella "Ahmed Ben Bella")'s socialist regime in Algeria during the [Sand War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sand_War "Sand War"). He also allied with [Alphonse Massamba-Débat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphonse_Massamba-D%C3%A9bat "Alphonse Massamba-Débat")'s socialist government in [Congo-Brazzaville](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congo-Brazzaville "Congo-Brazzaville"). In 1965, Castro authorized Che Guevara to travel to [Congo-Kinshasa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville) "Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)") to train [revolutionaries against the Western-backed government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simba_rebellion "Simba rebellion").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986255–256,_260Quirk1993744Coltman2003211–212_224-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986255%E2%80%93256,_260Quirk1993744Coltman2003211%E2%80%93212-224">[224]</a></sup> Castro was personally devastated when Guevara was killed by CIA-backed troops in Bolivia in October 1967 and publicly attributed it to Guevara's disregard for his own safety.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986267–268Quirk1993582–585Coltman2003216_225-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986267%E2%80%93268Quirk1993582%E2%80%93585Coltman2003216-225">[225]</a></sup>

In 1966, Castro staged a [Tri-Continental Conference of Africa, Asia and Latin America](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_Solidarity_with_the_People_of_Asia,_Africa_and_Latin_America "Organization of Solidarity with the People of Asia, Africa and Latin America") in Havana, further establishing himself as a significant player on the world stage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986265Coltman2003214_226-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986265Coltman2003214-226">[226]</a></sup> From this conference, Castro created the Latin American Solidarity Organization (OLAS), which adopted the slogan of "The duty of a revolution is to make revolution", signifying Havana's leadership of Latin America's revolutionary movement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986267_227-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986267-227">[227]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fidel-Gagarin-hug.jpg)

Castro and Russian cosmonaut [Yuri Gagarin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin "Yuri Gagarin"), the first human in space

Castro's increasing role on the world stage strained his relationship with the USSR, now under the leadership of [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev "Leonid Brezhnev"). Asserting Cuba's independence, Castro refused to sign the [Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons "Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons"), declaring it a Soviet-US attempt to dominate the [Third World](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_World "Third World").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986269_228-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986269-228">[228]</a></sup> Diverting from Soviet Marxist doctrine, he suggested that Cuban society could evolve straight to [pure communism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_communism "Pure communism") rather than gradually progress through various stages of socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993559–560_229-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993559%E2%80%93560-229">[229]</a></sup> In turn, the Soviet-loyalist Aníbal Escalante began organizing a government network of opposition to Castro, though in January 1968, he and his supporters were arrested for allegedly passing state secrets to Moscow.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986269–270Quirk1993588–590_230-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986269%E2%80%93270Quirk1993588%E2%80%93590-230">[230]</a></sup> Recognising Cuba's economic dependence on the Soviets, Castro relented to Brezhnev's pressure to be obedient, and in August 1968 he denounced the leaders of the [Prague Spring](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague_Spring "Prague Spring") and praised the [Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia "Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986270–271Quirk1993597–600Coltman2003216–217_231-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986270%E2%80%93271Quirk1993597%E2%80%93600Coltman2003216%E2%80%93217-231">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup>

Influenced by China's [Great Leap Forward](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward "Great Leap Forward"), in 1968 Castro proclaimed a [Great Revolutionary Offensive](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutionary_Offensive "Revolutionary Offensive"), closing all remaining privately owned shops and businesses and denouncing their owners as capitalist counterrevolutionaries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993591–594Coltman2003227_233-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993591%E2%80%93594Coltman2003227-233">[233]</a></sup> The severe lack of consumer goods for purchase led productivity to decline, as large sectors of the population felt little incentive to work hard.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993647_234-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993647-234">[234]</a></sup> This was exacerbated by the perception that a revolutionary elite had emerged, consisting of those connected to the administration; they had access to better housing, private transportation, servants, and the ability to purchase luxury goods abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993644–645_235-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993644%E2%80%93645-235">[235]</a></sup>

### Economic stagnation and Third World politics: 1969–1974

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:BENZAZA_BOUMEDIENE_CASTRO.jpg)

Late President of Algeria [Houari Boumediene](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houari_Boum%C3%A9di%C3%A8ne "Houari Boumédiène"), Fidel Castro, and Benzaza Hadj Benabdallah – May 1972

Castro publicly celebrated his administration's 10th anniversary in January 1969; in his celebratory speech he warned of sugar rations, reflecting the nation's economic problems.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993618–621Coltman2003227_236-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993618%E2%80%93621Coltman2003227-236">[236]</a></sup> The 1969 crop was heavily damaged by a hurricane, and to meet its export quota, the government drafted in the army, implemented a seven-day working week, and postponed public holidays to lengthen the harvest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986273Quirk1993634–640Coltman2003229_237-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986273Quirk1993634%E2%80%93640Coltman2003229-237">[237]</a></sup> When that year's production quota was not met, Castro offered to resign during a public speech, but assembled crowds insisted he remain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986274Quirk1993644Coltman2003230_238-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986274Quirk1993644Coltman2003230-238">[238]</a></sup> Despite the economic issues, many of Castro's social reforms were popular, with the population largely supportive of the "Achievements of the Revolution" in education, medical care, housing, and road construction, as well as the policies of "direct democratic" public consultation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986275–276Quirk1993606Coltman2003230_239-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986275%E2%80%93276Quirk1993606Coltman2003230-239">[239]</a></sup> Seeking Soviet help, from 1970 to 1972 Soviet economists re-organized Cuba's economy, founding the Cuban-Soviet Commission of Economic, Scientific and Technical Collaboration, while Soviet premier [Alexei Kosygin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexei_Kosygin "Alexei Kosygin") visited in October 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986276–277Quirk1993682–684_240-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986276%E2%80%93277Quirk1993682%E2%80%93684-240">[240]</a></sup> In July 1972, Cuba joined the [Council for Mutual Economic Assistance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comecon "Comecon") (Comecon), an economic organization of socialist states, although this further limited Cuba's economy to agricultural production.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986277_241-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986277-241">[241]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L0614-040,_Berlin,_Fidel_Castro_an_der_Grenze.jpg)

Castro and members of the East German [Politburo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politburo "Politburo") in Berlin, June 1972

In May 1970, the crews of two Cuban fishing boats were kidnapped by Florida-based dissident group [Alpha 66](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpha_66 "Alpha 66"), who demanded that Cuba release imprisoned militants. Under US pressure, the hostages were released, and Castro welcomed them back as heroes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993640–641Coltman2003230_242-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993640%E2%80%93641Coltman2003230-242">[242]</a></sup> In April 1971, Castro was internationally condemned for ordering the arrest of dissident poet [Heberto Padilla](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heberto_Padilla "Heberto Padilla") who had been arrested 20 March; Padilla was freed, but the government established the National Cultural Council to ensure that intellectuals and artists supported the administration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993609–615,_662–676Coltman2003232–233_243-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993609%E2%80%93615,_662%E2%80%93676Coltman2003232%E2%80%93233-243">[243]</a></sup>

In November 1971, [Castro visited Chile](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_visit_by_Fidel_Castro_to_Chile "State visit by Fidel Castro to Chile"), where Marxist President [Salvador Allende](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salvador_Allende "Salvador Allende") had been elected as the head of [a left-wing coalition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Unity_(Chile) "Popular Unity (Chile)"). Castro supported Allende's socialist reforms but warned him of right-wing elements in Chile's military. In 1973, the military [led a coup d'état](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_Chilean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1973 Chilean coup d'état") and established a military junta led by [Augusto Pinochet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet "Augusto Pinochet").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986278–280Quirk1993685–701,_703Coltman2003233–236,_240_244-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986278%E2%80%93280Quirk1993685%E2%80%93701,_703Coltman2003233%E2%80%93236,_240-244">[244]</a></sup> Castro proceeded to Guinea to meet socialist President [Sékou Touré](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9 "Sékou Touré"), praising him as Africa's greatest leader, and there received the [Order of Fidelity to the People](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Fidelity_to_the_People "Order of Fidelity to the People").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993706–707Coltman2003237–238_245-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993706%E2%80%93707Coltman2003237%E2%80%93238-245">[245]</a></sup> He then went on a seven-week tour visiting leftist allies: Algeria, Bulgaria, Hungary, Poland, East Germany, Czechoslovakia and the Soviet Union, where he was given further awards. On each trip, he was eager to visit factory and farm workers, publicly praising their governments; privately, he urged the regimes to aid revolutionary movements elsewhere, particularly those fighting the [Vietnam War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War "Vietnam War").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993707–715Coltman2003238_246-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993707%E2%80%93715Coltman2003238-246">[246]</a></sup>

In September 1973, he returned to [Algiers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers "Algiers") to attend the Fourth Summit of the [Non-Aligned Movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement "Non-Aligned Movement") (NAM). Various NAM members were critical of Castro's attendance, claiming that Cuba was aligned to the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact") and therefore should not be at the conference.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986283–284Quirk1993718–719Coltman2003239_247-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986283%E2%80%93284Quirk1993718%E2%80%93719Coltman2003239-247">[247]</a></sup> At the conference he publicly broke off relations with Israel, citing its government's close relationship with the US and its treatment of Palestinians during the [Israel–Palestine conflict](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict "Israeli–Palestinian conflict"). This earned Castro respect throughout the Arab world, in particular from the Libyan leader [Muammar Gaddafi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi "Muammar Gaddafi"), who became a friend and ally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993721Coltman2003239–240_248-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993721Coltman2003239%E2%80%93240-248">[248]</a></sup> As the [Yom Kippur War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War "Yom Kippur War") broke out in October 1973 between Israel and an Arab coalition led by Egypt and Syria, Cuba sent 4,000 troops to aid Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986284Quirk1993745–746_249-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986284Quirk1993745%E2%80%93746-249">[249]</a></sup> Leaving Algiers, Castro visited Iraq and [North Vietnam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Vietnam "North Vietnam").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993721–723_250-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993721%E2%80%93723-250">[250]</a></sup>

Cuba's economy grew in 1974 as a result of high international sugar prices and new credits with Argentina, Canada, and parts of Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986283–284Quirk1993724–725Coltman2003240_251-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986283%E2%80%93284Quirk1993724%E2%80%93725Coltman2003240-251">[251]</a></sup> A number of Latin American states called for Cuba's re-admittance into the Organization of American States (OAS), with the US finally conceding in 1975 on [Henry Kissinger](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Kissinger "Henry Kissinger")'s advice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986282Quirk1993737_252-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986282Quirk1993737-252">[252]</a></sup> Cuba's government underwent a restructuring along Soviet lines, claiming that this would further democratization and decentralize power away from Castro. Officially announcing Cuba's identity as a [socialist state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_state "Socialist state"), the first National Congress of the Cuban Communist Party was held, and [a new constitution drafted](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Cuba#1976_Constitution "Constitution of Cuba") that abolished the position of president and prime minister. Castro remained the dominant figure in governance, taking the presidency of the newly created [Council of State](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_State_(Cuba) "Council of State (Cuba)") and [Council of Ministers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Cuba) "Council of Ministers (Cuba)"), making him both [head of state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state") and head of government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986283Quirk1993726–729Coltman2003240–241_253-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986283Quirk1993726%E2%80%93729Coltman2003240%E2%80%93241-253">[253]</a></sup>

## Presidency

### Foreign wars and NAM Presidency: 1975–1979

Castro considered Africa to be "the weakest link in the imperialist chain", and at the request of [Agostinho Neto](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agostinho_Neto "Agostinho Neto") he ordered 230 military advisers into [Angola](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Angola "People's Republic of Angola") in November 1975 to aid Neto's Marxist [MPLA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/MPLA "MPLA") in the [Angolan Civil War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War "Angolan Civil War"). When the US and South Africa stepped up their support of the opposition [FLNA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_of_Angola "National Liberation Front of Angola") and [UNITA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNITA "UNITA"), Castro ordered a further 18,000 troops to Angola, which played a major role in forcing a South African and UNITA retreat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986281,_284–287Quirk1993747–750Coltman2003242–243_254-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986281,_284%E2%80%93287Quirk1993747%E2%80%93750Coltman2003242%E2%80%93243-254">[254]</a></sup> The decision to intervene in Angola has been a controversial one, all the more so as Castro's critics have charged that it was not his decision at all, contending that the Soviets ordered him to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge200477–79_255-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge200477%E2%80%9379-255">[255]</a></sup> Castro always maintained that he took the decision to launch Operation Carlota himself in response to an appeal from Neto and that the Soviets were in fact opposed to Cuban intervention in Angola, which took place over their opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge200479_256-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge200479-256">[256]</a></sup>

Traveling to Angola, Castro celebrated with Neto, Sékou Touré and Guinea-Bissaun president [Luís Cabral](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Cabral "Luís Cabral"), where they agreed to support Mozambique's [Marxist–Leninist government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/FRELIMO "FRELIMO") against [RENAMO](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/RENAMO "RENAMO") in the [Mozambican Civil War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozambican_Civil_War "Mozambican Civil War").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993752Coltman2003243_257-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993752Coltman2003243-257">[257]</a></sup> In February, Castro visited Algeria and then Libya, where he spent ten days with Gaddafi and oversaw the establishment of the [Jamahariya system of governance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi#Great_Socialist_People's_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya_(1977%E2%80%932011) "History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi"), before attending talks with [the Marxist government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yemeni_Socialist_Party "Yemeni Socialist Party") of [South Yemen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Yemen "South Yemen"). From there he proceeded to Somalia, Tanzania, Mozambique and Angola where he was greeted by crowds as a hero for Cuba's role in opposing apartheid South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993759–761Coltman2003243–244_258-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993759%E2%80%93761Coltman2003243%E2%80%93244-258">[258]</a></sup> Throughout much of Africa he was hailed as a friend to national liberation from foreign dominance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993750_259-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993750-259">[259]</a></sup> This was followed with visits to East Berlin and Moscow.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993766–767_260-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993766%E2%80%93767-260">[260]</a></sup>

> There is often talk of human rights, but it is also necessary to talk of the rights of humanity. Why should some people walk barefoot, so that others can travel in luxurious cars? Why should some live for thirty-five years, so that others can live for seventy years? Why should some be miserably poor, so that others can be hugely rich? I speak on behalf of the children in the world who do not have a piece of bread. I speak on the behalf of the sick who have no medicine, of those whose rights to life and human dignity have been denied.

– Fidel Castro's message to the UN General Assembly, 1979<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003245_261-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003245-261">[261]</a></sup>

In 1977, the [Ogaden War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ogaden_War "Ogaden War") broke out over the disputed [Ogaden](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ogaden "Ogaden") region as Somalia invaded Ethiopia; although a former ally of Somali president [Siad Barre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siad_Barre "Siad Barre"), Castro had warned him against such action, and Cuba sided with [Mengistu Haile Mariam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mengistu_Haile_Mariam "Mengistu Haile Mariam")'s Marxist government of Ethiopia. In a desperate attempt to stop the war, Castro had a summit with Barre where he proposed a federation of Ethiopia, Somalia, and South Yemen as an alternative to war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETareke2009190_262-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTETareke2009190-262">[262]</a></sup> Barre who saw seizing the Ogaden as the first step towards creating a greater Somalia that would unite all of the Somalis into one state rejected the federation offer and decided upon war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETareke2009190_262-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTETareke2009190-262">[262]</a></sup> Castro sent troops under the command of General [Arnaldo Ochoa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arnaldo_Ochoa "Arnaldo Ochoa") to aid the overwhelmed Ethiopian army. Mengistu's regime was barely hanging on by 1977, having lost one-third of its army in Eritrea at the time of the Somali invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrogan198931_263-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrogan198931-263">[263]</a></sup> The intervention of 17,000 Cuban troops into the Ogaden was by all accounts decisive in altering a war that Ethiopia was on the brink of losing into a victory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrogan198931–34_264-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrogan198931%E2%80%9334-264">[264]</a></sup>

After forcing back the Somalis, Mengistu then ordered the Ethiopians to suppress the [Eritrean People's Liberation Front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eritrean_People%27s_Liberation_Front "Eritrean People's Liberation Front"), a measure Castro refused to support.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986291–292Quirk1993761–765,_776–781Coltman2003245_265-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986291%E2%80%93292Quirk1993761%E2%80%93765,_776%E2%80%93781Coltman2003245-265">[265]</a></sup> Castro extended support to Latin American revolutionary movements, namely the [Sandinista National Liberation Front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front "Sandinista National Liberation Front") in its overthrow of the Nicaraguan rightist government of [Anastasio Somoza Debayle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle "Anastasio Somoza Debayle") in July 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003249_266-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003249-266">[266]</a></sup> Castro's critics accused the government of wasting Cuban lives in these military endeavours; the anti-Castro [Center for a Free Cuba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_for_a_Free_Cuba "Center for a Free Cuba") has claimed that an estimated 14,000 Cubans were killed in foreign Cuban military actions.<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> When American critics claimed that Castro had no right to interfere in these nations, he countered that Cuba had been invited into them, pointing out the US's own involvement in various foreign nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993759_268-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993759-268">[268]</a></sup> Between 1979 and 1991 about 370,000 Cuban troops together with 50,000 Cuban civilians (mostly teachers and doctors) served in Angola, representing about 5% of Cuba's population.<sup id="cite_ref-Vines_269-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Vines-269">[269]</a></sup> The Cuban intervention in Angola was envisioned as a short-term commitment, but the Angolan government used the profits from the oil industry to subsidize Cuba's economy, making Cuba as economically dependent upon Angola as Angola was militarily dependent upon Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-Vines_269-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Vines-269">[269]</a></sup>

In the late 1970s, Cuba's relations with North American states improved during the period with Mexican president [Luis Echeverría](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luis_Echeverr%C3%ADa "Luis Echeverría"), Canadian prime minister [Pierre Trudeau](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau "Pierre Trudeau"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993750–751Coltman2003244–245_270-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993750%E2%80%93751Coltman2003244%E2%80%93245-270">[270]</a></sup> and US president [Jimmy Carter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter "Jimmy Carter") in power. Carter continued criticizing Cuba's human rights abuses but adopted a respectful approach which gained Castro's attention. Considering Carter well-meaning and sincere, Castro freed certain political prisoners and allowed some Cuban exiles to visit relatives on the island, hoping that in turn Carter would abolish the economic embargo and stop CIA support for militant dissidents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986289Quirk1993756–759,_769,_771Coltman2003247–248_271-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986289Quirk1993756%E2%80%93759,_769,_771Coltman2003247%E2%80%93248-271">[271]</a></sup> Conversely, his relationship with China declined, as he accused [Deng Xiaoping](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping "Deng Xiaoping")'s Chinese government of betraying their revolutionary principles by initiating trade links with the US and [attacking Vietnam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Vietnamese_War "Sino-Vietnamese War").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993793–794_272-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993793%E2%80%93794-272">[272]</a></sup> In 1979, the Conference of the Non-Aligned Movement (NAM) was held in Havana, where Castro was selected as NAM president, a position he held until 1982. In his capacity as both president of the NAM and of Cuba he appeared at the United Nations General Assembly in October 1979 and gave a speech on the disparity between the world's rich and poor. His speech was greeted with much applause from other world leaders,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986294Quirk1993782–783,_798–802Coltman2003245_273-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986294Quirk1993782%E2%80%93783,_798%E2%80%93802Coltman2003245-273">[273]</a></sup> though his standing in NAM was damaged by Cuba's refusal to condemn the [Soviet intervention in Afghanistan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Afghan–Soviet War").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986294_274-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986294-274">[274]</a></sup>

### Reagan and Gorbachev: 1980–1991

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fidel_Castro,_Havana,_1978_(9609361).jpg)

Castro speaking in Havana, 1978

By the 1980s, Cuba's economy was again in trouble, following a decline in the market price of sugar and 1979's decimated harvest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993754–755,_804Coltman2003250Gott2004288_275-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993754%E2%80%93755,_804Coltman2003250Gott2004288-275">[275]</a></sup> For the first time, unemployment became a serious problem in Castro's Cuba, with the government sending unemployed youth to other countries, primarily East Germany, to work there.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993804,_816_276-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993804,_816-276">[276]</a></sup> Desperate for money, Cuba's government secretly sold off paintings from national collections and illicitly traded for US electronic goods through Panama.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003255_277-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003255-277">[277]</a></sup> Increasing numbers of Cubans fled to Florida but were labelled "scum" and "[lumpen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lumpenproletariat "Lumpenproletariat")" by Castro and his CDR supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993808Coltman2003250–251_278-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993808Coltman2003250%E2%80%93251-278">[278]</a></sup> In one incident, 10,000 Cubans stormed the Peruvian Embassy requesting asylum, and so the US agreed that it would accept 3,500 refugees. Castro conceded that those who wanted to leave could do so from Mariel port. In what was known as the [Mariel boatlift](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariel_boatlift "Mariel boatlift"), hundreds of boats arrived from the US, leading to a mass exodus of 120,000; Castro's government took advantage of the situation by loading criminals, the mentally ill, and homosexuals onto the boats destined for Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986295Quirk1993807–810Coltman2003251–252_279-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986295Quirk1993807%E2%80%93810Coltman2003251%E2%80%93252-279">[279]</a></sup> The event destabilized Carter's administration, and later, in 1980, [Ronald Reagan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") was elected US president.

Reagan's administration adopted a hard-line approach against Castro, making its desire to overthrow his regime clear.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986296Quirk1993810–815Coltman2003252_280-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986296Quirk1993810%E2%80%93815Coltman2003252-280">[280]</a></sup> In late 1981, Castro publicly accused the US of biological warfare against Cuba by orchestrating a [dengue fever](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dengue_fever "Dengue fever") epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993812–813Coltman2003252_281-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993812%E2%80%93813Coltman2003252-281">[281]</a></sup> Cuba's economy became even more dependent on Soviet aid, with Soviet subsidies (mainly in the form of supplies of low-cost oil and voluntarily buying Cuban sugar at inflated prices) averaging $4–5 billion a year by the late 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-282"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> This accounted for 30–38% of the country's entire GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> Soviet economic assistance had not helped Cuba's long-term growth prospects by promoting diversification or sustainability. Although described as a "relatively highly developed Latin American export economy" in 1959 and the early 1960s, Cuba's basic economic structure changed very little between then and the 1980s. Tobacco products such as cigars and cigarettes were the only manufactured products among Cuba's leading exports and were produced using an expensive and labor-intensive pre-industrial process. The Cuban economy remained highly inefficient and over-specialized in a few highly subsidized commodities exported primarily to the [Soviet bloc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_bloc "Soviet bloc") countries.<sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup>

Although despising Argentina's [right-wing military junta](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Reorganization_Process "National Reorganization Process"), Castro supported them in the 1982 [Falklands War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falklands_War "Falklands War") against Britain and offered military aid to the Argentinians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003253_285-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003253-285">[285]</a></sup> Castro supported the leftist [New Jewel Movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Jewel_Movement "New Jewel Movement") that seized power in [Grenada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Revolutionary_Government "People's Revolutionary Government") in 1979, befriending Grenadine president [Maurice Bishop](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maurice_Bishop "Maurice Bishop") and sending doctors, teachers, and technicians to aid the country's development. When Bishop was executed in a Soviet-backed coup by hard-line Marxist [Bernard Coard](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernard_Coard "Bernard Coard") in October 1983, Castro condemned the killing but cautiously retained support for Grenada's government. However, the US used the coup as a basis for [invading the island](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada "United States invasion of Grenada"). Cuban soldiers died in the conflict, with Castro denouncing the invasion and comparing the US to [Nazi Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986297Quirk1993819–822Coltman2003253–254_286-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986297Quirk1993819%E2%80%93822Coltman2003253%E2%80%93254-286">[286]</a></sup> In a July 1983 speech marking the 30th anniversary of the Cuban Revolution, Castro condemned Reagan's administration as a "reactionary, extremist clique" who were waging an "openly warmongering and fascist foreign policy".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993818_287-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993818-287">[287]</a></sup> Castro feared a [US invasion of Nicaragua](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA_activities_in_Nicaragua "CIA activities in Nicaragua") and sent Ochoa to train the governing [Sandinistas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandinistas "Sandinistas") in guerrilla warfare but received little support from the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003254–255_288-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003254%E2%80%93255-288">[288]</a></sup>

In 1985, [Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev") became Secretary-General of the Soviet Communist Party; a reformer, he implemented measures to increase freedom of the press (_[glasnost](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glasnost "Glasnost")_) and economic decentralization (_[perestroika](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perestroika "Perestroika")_) in an attempt to strengthen socialism. Like many orthodox Marxist critics, Castro feared that the reforms would weaken the socialist state and allow capitalist elements to regain control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993826Coltman2003256Gott2004273_289-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993826Coltman2003256Gott2004273-289">[289]</a></sup> Gorbachev conceded to US demands to reduce support for Cuba,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003256_290-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003256-290">[290]</a></sup> with Soviet-Cuban relations deteriorating.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003257_291-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003257-291">[291]</a></sup> On medical advice given him in October 1985, Castro gave up regularly smoking [Cuban cigars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_cigar "Cuban cigar"), helping to set an example for the rest of the populace.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003224_292-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003224-292">[292]</a></sup> Castro became passionate in his denunciation of the Third World debt problem, arguing that the Third World would never escape the debt that First World banks and governments imposed upon it. In 1985, Havana hosted five international conferences on the world debt problem.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003255_277-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003255-277">[277]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lobito_Lighthouse_1995.jpg)

Castro's image painted onto a now-destroyed lighthouse in [Lobito](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lobito "Lobito"), Angola, 1995

By November 1987, Castro began spending more time on the Angolan Civil War, in which the Marxist MPLA government had fallen into retreat. Angolan president [José Eduardo dos Santos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos "José Eduardo dos Santos") successfully appealed for more Cuban troops, with Castro later admitting that he devoted more time to Angola than to the domestic situation, believing that a victory would lead to the collapse of apartheid. In response to the [siege of Cuito Cuanavale](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Cuito_Cuanavale "Battle of Cuito Cuanavale") in 1987–1988 by South African–UNITA forces, Castro sent an additional 12,000 Cuban Army troops to Angola in late 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899_293-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899-293">[293]</a></sup> From afar in Havana, Castro was closely involved in the decision-making about the defence of Cuito Cuanavle and came into conflict with Ochoa, whom he criticized for almost losing Cuito Cuanavle to a South African-UNITA assault on 13 January 1988 despite warning for almost two months prior that such an attack was coming.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004220_294-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004220-294">[294]</a></sup> On 30 January 1988, Ochoa was summoned to a meeting with Castro in Havana where he was told that Cuito Cuanavale must not fall and to execute Castro's plans for a pull-back to more defensible positions over the objections of the Angolans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004221_295-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004221-295">[295]</a></sup> The Cuban troops played a decisive role in the relief of Cuito Cuanavale, breaking the siege in March 1988, which led to the withdrawal of most of the South African troops from Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899_293-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899-293">[293]</a></sup> Cuban propaganda turned the siege of Cuito Cuanavle into a decisive victory that changed the course of African history and Castro awarded 82 soldiers medals of the newly created Medal of Merit for the Defense of Cuito Cuanavle on 1 April 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004234–235_296-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004234%E2%80%93235-296">[296]</a></sup> Tensions were increased with the Cubans advancing close to the border of Namibia, which led to warnings from the South African government that they considered this an extremely unfriendly act, causing South Africa to mobilize and call up its reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899_293-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899-293">[293]</a></sup> In the spring of 1988, the intensity of South African-Cuban fighting drastically increased with both sides taking heavy losses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004237–239_297-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004237%E2%80%93239-297">[297]</a></sup>

The prospect of an all-out Cuban-South African war served to concentrate minds in both Moscow and Washington and led to an increased push for a diplomatic solution to the Angolan war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899_293-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899-293">[293]</a></sup> The cost of Cuba's wars in Africa were paid for with Soviet subsidies at a time when the Soviet economy was badly hurt by low oil prices while the apartheid government of South Africa had by the 1980s become a very awkward American ally as much of the American population, especially black Americans, objected to apartheid. From the viewpoint of both Moscow and Washington, having both Cuba and South Africa disengage in Angola was the best possible outcome.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899_293-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrogan19899-293">[293]</a></sup> The low oil prices of the 1980s had also changed the Angolan attitude about subsidizing the Cuban economy as dos Santos found the promises made in the 1970s when oil prices were high to be a serious drain upon Angola's economy in the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Vines_269-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Vines-269">[269]</a></sup> South African whites were vastly outnumbered by South African blacks, and accordingly the South African Army could not take heavy losses with its white troops as that would fatally weaken the ability of the South African state to uphold apartheid.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004234_298-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004234-298">[298]</a></sup> The Cubans had also taken heavy losses while the increasing difficult relations with dos Santos who become less generous in subsidizing the Cuban economy suggested that such losses were not worth the cost.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004246_299-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge2004246-299">[299]</a></sup> Gorbachev called for a negotiated end to the conflict and in 1988 organized a quadripartite talk between the USSR, US, Cuba and South Africa; they agreed that all foreign troops would pull out of Angola while South Africa agreed to grant independence to Namibia. Castro was angered by Gorbachev's approach, believing that he was abandoning the plight of the world's poor in favour of détente.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003257–258Gott2004276–279_300-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003257%E2%80%93258Gott2004276%E2%80%93279-300">[300]</a></sup>

When Gorbachev visited Cuba in April 1989, he informed Castro that _perestroika_ meant an end to subsidies for Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993827–828Coltman2003260–261Gott2004276_301-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993827%E2%80%93828Coltman2003260%E2%80%93261Gott2004276-301">[301]</a></sup> Ignoring calls for liberalization in accordance with the Soviet example, Castro continued to clamp down on internal dissidents and in particular kept tabs on the military, the primary threat to the government. A number of senior military officers, including Ochoa and [Tony de la Guardia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_de_la_Guardia "Tony de la Guardia"), were investigated for corruption and complicity in cocaine smuggling, tried, and executed in 1989, despite calls for leniency.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993828–829Coltman2003258–266Gott2004279–286_302-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993828%E2%80%93829Coltman2003258%E2%80%93266Gott2004279%E2%80%93286-302">[302]</a></sup> In Eastern Europe, socialist governments fell to capitalist reformers between 1989 and 1991 and many Western observers expected the same in Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993830Coltman2003277Gott2004286_303-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993830Coltman2003277Gott2004286-303">[303]</a></sup> Increasingly isolated, Cuba improved relations with [Manuel Noriega](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Noriega "Manuel Noriega")'s right-wing government in Panama—despite Castro's personal hatred of Noriega—but it was overthrown in a US invasion in December 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003267–268Gott2004286_304-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003267%E2%80%93268Gott2004286-304">[304]</a></sup> In February 1990, Castro's allies in Nicaragua, President [Daniel Ortega](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Ortega "Daniel Ortega") and the Sandinistas, were defeated by the US-funded [National Opposition Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Opposition_Union "National Opposition Union") in an election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003268–270Gott2004286_305-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003268%E2%80%93270Gott2004286-305">[305]</a></sup> With the collapse of the Soviet bloc, the US secured a majority vote for a resolution condemning Cuba's human rights violations at the [United Nations Human Rights Commission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Commission "United Nations Human Rights Commission") in Geneva, Switzerland. Cuba asserted that this was a manifestation of US hegemony and refused to allow an investigative delegation to enter the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993831Coltman2003270–271_306-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993831Coltman2003270%E2%80%93271-306">[306]</a></sup>

### Special Period: 1992–2000

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cuba.FidelCastro.02.jpg)

Castro in front of a Havana statue of Cuban national hero [José Martí](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD "José Martí") in 2003

With favourable trade from the Soviet bloc ended, Castro publicly declared that Cuba was entering a "[Special Period in Time of Peace](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Period_in_Time_of_Peace "Special Period in Time of Peace")". Petrol rations were dramatically reduced, Chinese bicycles were imported to replace cars, and factories performing non-essential tasks were shut down. Oxen began to replace tractors; firewood began being used for cooking and electricity cuts were introduced that lasted 16 hours a day. Castro admitted that Cuba faced the worst situation short of open war, and that the country might have to resort to [subsistence farming](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subsistence_farming "Subsistence farming").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993830–831Balfour1995163Coltman2003271Gott2004287–289_307-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993830%E2%80%93831Balfour1995163Coltman2003271Gott2004287%E2%80%93289-307">[307]</a></sup> By 1992, Cuba's economy had declined by over 40% in under two years, with major food shortages, widespread malnutrition and a lack of basic goods.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003282Gott2004288_308-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003282Gott2004288-308">[308]</a></sup> Castro hoped for a restoration of Marxism–Leninism in the USSR but refrained from backing the [1991 coup in that country](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt "1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003274–275_309-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003274%E2%80%93275-309">[309]</a></sup> When Gorbachev regained control, Cuba-Soviet relations deteriorated further, and Soviet troops were withdrawn in September 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993832–833Coltman2003275_310-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993832%E2%80%93833Coltman2003275-310">[310]</a></sup> In December, the [Soviet Union was officially dissolved](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union") as [Boris Yeltsin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin "Boris Yeltsin") abolished the Soviet Communist Party and introducing a capitalist [multiparty democracy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiparty_democracy "Multiparty democracy"). Yeltsin despised Castro and developed links with the Miami-based [Cuban American National Foundation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_American_National_Foundation "Cuban American National Foundation").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993832Coltman2003274–275_311-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993832Coltman2003274%E2%80%93275-311">[311]</a></sup> Castro tried improving relations with the capitalist nations. He welcomed Western politicians and investors to Cuba, befriended [Manuel Fraga](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Fraga "Manuel Fraga") and took a particular interest in [Margaret Thatcher](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher "Margaret Thatcher")'s policies in the UK, believing that Cuban socialism could learn from her emphasis on low taxation and personal initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003290–291_312-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003290%E2%80%93291-312">[312]</a></sup> He ceased support for foreign militants, refrained from praising [FARC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/FARC "FARC") on a 1994 visit to Colombia and called for a negotiated settlement between the [Zapatistas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zapatista_Army_of_National_Liberation "Zapatista Army of National Liberation") and Mexican government in 1995. Publicly, he presented himself as a moderate on the world stage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003305–306_313-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003305%E2%80%93306-313">[313]</a></sup>

In 1991, Havana [hosted](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Pan_American_Games "1991 Pan American Games") the [Pan American Games](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan_American_Games "Pan American Games"), which involved construction of [a stadium](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadio_Panamericano,_Havana "Estadio Panamericano, Havana") and accommodation for the athletes; Castro admitted that it was an expensive error, but it was a success for Cuba's government. Crowds regularly shouted "Fidel! Fidel!" in front of foreign journalists, while Cuba became the first Latin American nation to beat the US to the top of the gold-medal table.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993831–832Coltman2003272–273_314-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993831%E2%80%93832Coltman2003272%E2%80%93273-314">[314]</a></sup> Support for Castro remained strong, and although there were small anti-government demonstrations, the Cuban opposition rejected the exile community's calls for an armed uprising.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003275–276Gott2004314_315-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003275%E2%80%93276Gott2004314-315">[315]</a></sup> In August 1994, Havana witnessed the largest anti-Castro demonstration in Cuban history, as 200 to 300 young men threw stones at police, demanding that they be allowed to emigrate to Miami. A larger pro-Castro crowd confronted them, who were joined by Castro; he informed media that the men were anti-socials misled by the US. The protests dispersed with no recorded injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003297–299Gott2004298–299_316-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003297%E2%80%93299Gott2004298%E2%80%93299-316">[316]</a></sup> Fearing that dissident groups would invade, the government organized the "War of All the People" defence strategy, planning a widespread guerrilla warfare campaign, and the unemployed were given jobs building a network of bunkers and tunnels across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003287Gott2004273–274_317-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003287Gott2004273%E2%80%93274-317">[317]</a></sup>

> We do not have a smidgen of capitalism or neo-liberalism. We are facing a world completely ruled by neo-liberalism and capitalism. This does not mean that we are going to surrender. It means that we have to adopt to the reality of that world. That is what we are doing, with great equanimity, without giving up our ideals, our goals. I ask you to have trust in what the government and party are doing. They are defending, to the last atom, socialist ideas, principles and goals.

– Fidel Castro explaining the reforms of the Special Period<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003291–292_318-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003291%E2%80%93292-318">[318]</a></sup>

Castro believed in the need for reform if Cuban socialism was to survive in a world now dominated by capitalist free markets. In October 1991, the Fourth Congress of the Cuban Communist Party was held in Santiago, at which a number of important changes to the government were announced. Castro would step down as head of government, to be replaced by the much younger [Carlos Lage](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_Lage "Carlos Lage"), although Castro would remain the head of the Communist Party and commander-in-chief of the armed forces. Many older members of government were to be retired and replaced by their younger counterparts. A number of economic changes were proposed, and subsequently put to a national referendum. Free farmers' markets and small-scale private enterprises would be legalized in an attempt to stimulate economic growth, while US dollars were also made legal tender. Certain restrictions on emigration were eased, allowing more discontented Cuban citizens to move to the United States. Further democratization was to be brought in by having the National Assembly's members elected directly by the people, rather than through municipal and provincial assemblies. Castro welcomed debate between proponents and opponents of the [economics reforms](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_economic_reforms "Cuban economic reforms")—although over time he began to increasingly sympathise with the opponent's positions, arguing that such reforms must be delayed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003276–281,_284,_287Gott2004291–294_319-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003276%E2%80%93281,_284,_287Gott2004291%E2%80%93294-319">[319]</a></sup>
