Castro's government diversified its economy into [biotechnology](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biotechnology "Biotechnology") and [tourism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tourism_in_Cuba "Tourism in Cuba"), the latter outstripping Cuba's sugar industry as its primary source of revenue in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993836Coltman2003288Gott2004290,_322_320-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993836Coltman2003288Gott2004290,_322-320">[320]</a></sup> The arrival of thousands of Mexican and Spanish tourists led to increasing numbers of Cubans turning to prostitution; officially illegal, Castro refrained from cracking down on [prostitution in Cuba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prostitution_in_Cuba "Prostitution in Cuba"), fearing a political backlash.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003294_321-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003294-321">[321]</a></sup> Economic hardship led many Cubans toward religion, both in the form of [Roman Catholicism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholicism "Roman Catholicism") and [Santería](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa "Santería"). Although long thinking religious belief to be backward, Castro softened his approach to religious institutions and religious people were permitted for the first time to join the Communist Party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003278,_294–295Gott2004309_322-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003278,_294%E2%80%93295Gott2004309-322">[322]</a></sup> Although he viewed the Roman Catholic Church as a reactionary, pro-capitalist institution, Castro organized a visit to Cuba by [Pope John Paul II](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II "Pope John Paul II") for January 1998; it strengthened the position of both the Cuban Church and Castro's government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003309–311Gott2004306–310_323-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003309%E2%80%93311Gott2004306%E2%80%93310-323">[323]</a></sup>

In the early 1990s Castro embraced environmentalism, campaigning against [global warming](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_warming "Global warming") and the waste of natural resources and accusing the US of being the world's primary polluter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003312_324-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003312-324">[324]</a></sup> In 1994 a ministry dedicated to the environment was established, and new laws established in 1997 that promoted awareness of environmental issues throughout Cuba and stressed the sustainable use of natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhittleRey_Santos200677Evenson2010489,_502–503_325-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhittleRey_Santos200677Evenson2010489,_502%E2%80%93503-325">[325]</a></sup> By 2006, Cuba was the world's only nation which met the [United Nations Development Programme](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme "United Nations Development Programme")'s definition of sustainable development, with an [ecological footprint](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_footprint "Ecological footprint") of less than 1.8 hectares per capita and a [Human Development Index](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Index "Human Development Index") of over 0.8.<sup id="cite_ref-326"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> Castro also became a proponent of the [anti-globalization](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-globalization "Anti-globalization") movement, criticizing US global hegemony and the control exerted by [multinationals](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multinational_corporation "Multinational corporation").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003312_324-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003312-324">[324]</a></sup> Castro maintained his strong stance [against apartheid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_South_Africa_during_apartheid "Foreign relations of South Africa during apartheid"), and at the 26 July celebrations in 1991, he was joined onstage by [Nelson Mandela](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelson_Mandela "Nelson Mandela"), recently released from prison. Mandela praised Cuba's involvement in battling South Africa during the Angolan Civil War and thanked Castro personally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003283Gott2004279_327-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003283Gott2004279-327">[327]</a></sup> Castro later attended Mandela's inauguration as President of South Africa in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003304_328-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003304-328">[328]</a></sup> In 2001, Castro attended the Conference Against Racism in South Africa at which he lectured on the global spread of racial stereotypes through US film.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003312_324-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003312-324">[324]</a></sup>

### Pink tide: 2000–2006

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lula_anda_Castro9822.jpeg)

Castro meeting with Brazilian president [Lula da Silva](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lula_da_Silva "Lula da Silva"), a significant "[Pink Tide](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pink_Tide "Pink Tide")" leader

Mired in economic problems, Cuba was aided by [the election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_Venezuelan_presidential_election "1998 Venezuelan presidential election") of [Hugo Chávez](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez "Hugo Chávez") to the Venezuelan Presidency in 1999. Castro and Chávez developed a close friendship, with the former acting as a mentor and father-figure to the latter,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAzicri2009100MárquezSanabria2018138_329-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAzicri2009100M%C3%A1rquezSanabria2018138-329">[329]</a></sup> and together they built an alliance that had repercussions throughout Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAzicri2009100_330-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAzicri2009100-330">[330]</a></sup> In 2000, they signed an agreement through which Cuba would send 20,000 medics to Venezuela, in return receiving 53,000 barrels of oil per day at preferential rates; in 2004, this trade was stepped up, with Cuba sending 40,000 medics and Venezuela providing 90,000 barrels a day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarcanoBarrera_Tyszka2007213–215_331-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarcanoBarrera_Tyszka2007213%E2%80%93215-331">[331]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> Some economic problems remained; in 2004, Castro shut down 118 factories, including steel plants, sugar mills and paper processors to compensate for a critical shortage of fuel.<sup id="cite_ref-333"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> In September 2005, Castro established a group of medical professionals, known as the [Henry Reeve Brigade](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Reeve_Brigade "Henry Reeve Brigade"), with the mission of international medical solidarity. The group were sent throughout the world to carry out humanitarian missions on behalf of the Cuban government.<sup id="cite_ref-334"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup>

Cuba and Venezuela were the founding members of the [Bolivarian Alternative for the Americas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ALBA "ALBA") (ALBA).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAzicri2009100_330-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAzicri2009100-330">[330]</a></sup> ALBA's origins lay in a December 2004 agreement signed between the two countries and was formalized through a People's Trade Agreement also signed by [Evo Morales](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evo_Morales "Evo Morales")' Bolivia in April 2006. Castro had also been calling for greater Caribbean integration since the late 1990s, saying that only strengthened cooperation between Caribbean countries would prevent their domination by rich nations in a global economy.<sup id="cite_ref-335"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-336"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup> Cuba has opened four additional embassies in the [Caribbean Community](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean_Community "Caribbean Community") including: [Antigua and Barbuda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda "Antigua and Barbuda"), Dominica, [Suriname](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suriname "Suriname"), Saint Vincent and the Grenadines. This development makes Cuba the only country to have embassies in all independent countries of the Caribbean Community.<sup id="cite_ref-337"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fidel_Castro_1._Mai_2005_bei_Kundgebung.jpg)

Castro amid cheering crowds in 2005

In contrast to the improved relations between Cuba and a number of leftist Latin American states, in 2004 it broke off diplomatic ties with Panama after centrist President [Mireya Moscoso](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mireya_Moscoso "Mireya Moscoso") pardoned four Cuban exiles accused of attempting to assassinate Castro in 2000. Diplomatic ties were reinstalled in 2005 following the election of leftist President [Martín Torrijos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Torrijos "Martín Torrijos").<sup id="cite_ref-Cuba_and_Panama_restore_relations_338-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Cuba_and_Panama_restore_relations-338">[338]</a></sup> Castro's improving relations across Latin America were accompanied by continuing animosity towards the US. However, after massive damage caused by [Hurricane Michelle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurricane_Michelle "Hurricane Michelle") in 2001, Castro successfully proposed a one-time cash purchase of food from the US while declining its government's offer of humanitarian aid.<sup id="cite_ref-339"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup> Castro expressed solidarity with the US following the 2001 [September 11 attacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks "September 11 attacks"), condemning [Al-Qaeda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda "Al-Qaeda") and offering Cuban airports for the emergency diversion of any US planes. He recognized that the attacks would make US foreign policy more aggressive, which he believed was counterproductive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003320_340-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003320-340">[340]</a></sup> Castro criticized the [2003 invasion of Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq "2003 invasion of Iraq"), saying that the US-led war had imposed an international "law of the jungle".<sup id="cite_ref-341"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup>

Meanwhile, in 1998, Canadian prime minister [Jean Chrétien](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Chr%C3%A9tien "Jean Chrétien") arrived in Cuba to meet Castro and highlight their close ties. He was the first Canadian government leader to visit the island since Pierre Trudeau was in Havana in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup> In 2002, former US president Jimmy Carter visited Cuba, where he highlighted the lack of civil liberties in the country and urged the government to pay attention to the [Varela Project](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Varela_Project "Varela Project") of [Oswaldo Payá](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oswaldo_Pay%C3%A1 "Oswaldo Payá").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkierka2006xvi_343-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkierka2006xvi-343">[343]</a></sup>

## Final years

### Stepping down: 2006–2008

Castro underwent surgery for intestinal bleeding, and on 31 July 2006, [delegated his presidential](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006%E2%80%932008_Cuban_transfer_of_presidential_duties "2006–2008 Cuban transfer of presidential duties") duties to Raúl Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-344"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> In February 2007, Raúl announced that Fidel's health was improving and that he was taking part in important issues of government.<sup id="cite_ref-345"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup> Later that month, Fidel called into Hugo Chávez's radio show _[Aló Presidente](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al%C3%B3_Presidente "Aló Presidente")_.<sup id="cite_ref-346"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> On 21 April, Castro met [Wu Guanzheng](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wu_Guanzheng "Wu Guanzheng") of the [Chinese Communist Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party")'s [Politburo Standing Committee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politburo_Standing_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China "Politburo Standing Committee of the Communist Party of China"),<sup id="cite_ref-347"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup> with Chávez visiting in August,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarcanoBarrera_Tyszka2007287_348-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarcanoBarrera_Tyszka2007287-348">[348]</a></sup> and Morales in September.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESivak201052_349-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESivak201052-349">[349]</a></sup> That month, the Non-Aligned Movement held its 14th Summit in Havana, there agreeing to appoint Castro as the organization's president for a year's term.<sup id="cite_ref-350"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup>

Commenting on Castro's recovery, US president [George W. Bush](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_W._Bush "George W. Bush") said: "One day the good Lord will take Fidel Castro away." Hearing about this, the [atheist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheist "Atheist") Castro replied: "Now I understand why I survived Bush's plans and the plans of other presidents who ordered my assassination: the good Lord protected me." The quote was picked up on by the world's media.<sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup>

In a February 2008 letter, Castro announced that he would not accept the positions of President of the Council of State and Commander in Chief at that month's National Assembly meetings,<sup id="cite_ref-352"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup> remarking, "It would betray my conscience to take up a responsibility that requires mobility and total devotion, that I am not in a physical condition to offer".<sup id="cite_ref-353"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup> On 24 February 2008, the [National Assembly of People's Power](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_of_People%27s_Power "National Assembly of People's Power") unanimously voted Raúl as president.<sup id="cite_ref-354"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup> Describing his brother as "not substitutable", Raúl proposed that Fidel continue to be consulted on matters of great importance, a motion unanimously approved by the 597 National Assembly members.<sup id="cite_ref-355"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup>

### Retirement and final years: 2008–2016

Following his retirement, Castro's health deteriorated; international press speculated that he had [diverticulitis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diverticulitis "Diverticulitis"), but Cuba's government refused to corroborate this.<sup id="cite_ref-Franks_2012_356-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Franks_2012-356">[356]</a></sup> He continued to interact with the Cuban people, published an opinion column titled "Reflections" in _Granma_, used a Twitter account, and gave occasional public lectures.<sup id="cite_ref-Franks_2012_356-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Franks_2012-356">[356]</a></sup> In January 2009 Castro asked Cubans not to worry about his lack of recent news columns and failing health, and not to be disturbed by his future death.<sup id="cite_ref-357"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-357">[357]</a></sup> He continued meeting foreign leaders and dignitaries, and that month photographs were released of Castro's meeting with Argentine president [Cristina Fernández](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez "Cristina Fernández").<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_23Jan9_358-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-BBC_23Jan9-358">[358]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_y_Fidel_Castro.jpg)

Castro with Mexican president [Enrique Peña Nieto](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto "Enrique Peña Nieto"), January 2014; even in retirement, Castro continued his involvement with politics and international affairs.

In July 2010, he made his first public appearance since falling ill, greeting science center workers and giving a television interview to _[Mesa Redonda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesa_Redonda_Internacional "Mesa Redonda Internacional")_ in which he discussed US tensions with Iran and North Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-359"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-359">[359]</a></sup> On 7 August 2010, Castro gave his first speech to the National Assembly in four years, urging the US not to take military actions against those nations and warning of a [nuclear holocaust](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_holocaust "Nuclear holocaust").<sup id="cite_ref-360"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup> When asked whether Castro may be re-entering government, culture minister [Abel Prieto](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abel_Prieto "Abel Prieto") told the [BBC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC "BBC"), "I think that he has always been in Cuba's political life but he is not in the government ... He has been very careful about that. His big battle is international affairs."<sup id="cite_ref-361"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-361">[361]</a></sup>

On 19 April 2011, Castro resigned from the Communist Party central committee,<sup id="cite_ref-362"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-362">[362]</a></sup> thus stepping down as [First Secretary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_Cuba "First Secretary of the Communist Party of Cuba"). Raúl was selected as his successor.<sup id="cite_ref-363"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup> Now without any official role in the country's government, he took on the role of an elder [statesman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leader "Leader"). In March 2011, Castro condemned the [NATO-led military intervention in Libya](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya "2011 military intervention in Libya").<sup id="cite_ref-364"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup> In March 2012, [Pope Benedict XVI](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI "Pope Benedict XVI") visited Cuba for three days, during which time he briefly met with Castro despite the Pope's vocal opposition to Cuba's government.<sup id="cite_ref-Franks_2012_356-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Franks_2012-356">[356]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup> Later that year it was revealed that along with Hugo Chávez, Castro had played a significant behind-the-scenes role in orchestrating peace talks between the Colombian government and the far left FARC guerrilla movement to end the conflict which had raged since 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup> During the [North Korea crisis of 2013](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea_crisis_(2013) "North Korea crisis (2013)"), he urged both the North Korean and US governments to show restraint. Calling the situation "incredible and absurd", he maintained that war would not benefit either side, and that it represented "one of the gravest risks of nuclear war" since the Cuban missile crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-367"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup>

In December 2014, Castro was awarded the Chinese [Confucius Peace Prize](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confucius_Peace_Prize "Confucius Peace Prize") for seeking peaceful solutions to his nation's conflict with the US and for his post-retirement efforts to prevent nuclear war.<sup id="cite_ref-368"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup> In January 2015, he publicly commented on the "[Cuban Thaw](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Thaw "Cuban Thaw")", an increased normalization between Cuba-US relations, by stating that while it was a positive move for establishing peace in the region, he mistrusted the US government.<sup id="cite_ref-369"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup> He did not meet with US president [Barack Obama](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama "Barack Obama") on the latter's visit to Cuba in March 2016, although sent him a letter stating that Cuba "has no need of gifts from the empire".<sup id="cite_ref-370"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-370">[370]</a></sup> That April, he gave his most extensive public appearance in many years when addressing the Communist Party. Highlighting that he was soon to turn 90 years old, he noted that he would die in the near future but urged those assembled to retain their communist ideals.<sup id="cite_ref-371"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-371">[371]</a></sup> In September 2016, Castro was visited at his Havana home by the Iranian president [Hassan Rouhani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani "Hassan Rouhani"),<sup id="cite_ref-372"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-372">[372]</a></sup> and later that month was visited by Japanese prime minister [Shinzo Abe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shinzo_Abe "Shinzo Abe").<sup id="cite_ref-373"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup> In late October 2016, Castro met with the Portuguese president [Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcelo_Rebelo_de_Sousa "Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa"), who became one of the last foreign leaders to meet him.<sup id="cite_ref-374"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup>

### Death

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fidel_Castro%27s_funeral_procession.jpg)

Castro's funeral procession passing through [Sancti Spíritus Province](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sancti_Sp%C3%ADritus_Province "Sancti Spíritus Province"), Cuba

Castro died in Havana on the night of 25 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-AlJazeeraobit_375-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-AlJazeeraobit-375">[375]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Davison_376-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Davison-376">[376]</a></sup> The cause of death was not disclosed.<sup id="cite_ref-377"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup> His brother, President Raúl Castro, confirmed the news in a brief speech: "The commander in chief of the Cuban revolution died at 22:29 \[[EST](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone "Eastern Time Zone")\] this evening."<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_378-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-bbc-378">[378]</a></sup> His death came nine months after his older brother [Ramón](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Castro_Ruz "Ramón Castro Ruz") died at the age of 91 in February. Fidel Castro was [cremated](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cremation "Cremation") the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_378-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-bbc-378">[378]</a></sup> A funeral procession travelled 900 kilometres (560 mi) along the island's [central highway](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carretera_Central_(Cuba) "Carretera Central (Cuba)") from Havana to Santiago de Cuba, tracing in reverse the route of the "Freedom Caravan" of January 1959. After nine days of public mourning, his ashes were entombed in the [Santa Ifigenia Cemetery](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Ifigenia_Cemetery "Santa Ifigenia Cemetery") in Santiago de Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-379"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup>

## Ideology

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:XXX_Cumbre_del_Mercosur_-_C%C3%B3rdoba_-_21JUL06_-2-_presidenciagovar..jpg)

Castro (second from left) with South American leaders of the [Mercosur](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercosur "Mercosur") trade bloc in 2006. In the 2000s, Castro forged alliances in the Latin American "[pink tide](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pink_tide "Pink tide")".

Castro proclaimed himself to be "a [Socialist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist "Socialist"), a [Marxist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist "Marxist"), and a [Leninist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leninist "Leninist")",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009157_380-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009157-380">[380]</a></sup> and publicly identified as a [Marxist–Leninist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist "Marxist–Leninist") from December 1961 onward.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESondrol1991608_381-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESondrol1991608-381">[381]</a></sup> As a Marxist, Castro sought to transform Cuba from a capitalist state to a socialist society and ultimately to a communist society. Influenced by Guevara, he suggested that Cuba could evade most stages of socialism and progress straight to communism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993559–560_229-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993559%E2%80%93560-229">[229]</a></sup> The Cuban Revolution nevertheless did not meet the Marxist assumption that socialism would be achieved through proletariat revolution, for most of the forces involved in Batista's overthrow were led by members of the Cuban middle-class.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995177–178_382-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995177%E2%80%93178-382">[382]</a></sup> According to Castro, a country could be regarded as socialist if its means of production were controlled by the state. In this way, his understanding of socialism was less about who controlled power in a country and more about the method of distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995178_383-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995178-383">[383]</a></sup>

Castro's government was also [nationalistic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalistic "Nationalistic"), with Castro declaring, "We are not only Marxist-Leninists, but also nationalists and patriots".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993790_384-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993790-384">[384]</a></sup> In this it drew upon a longstanding tradition of Cuban nationalism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995177_385-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995177-385">[385]</a></sup> Castro biographer [Sebastian Balfour](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sebastian_Balfour "Sebastian Balfour") noted that "the vein of moral regeneration and voluntarism that runs through" Castro's thought owes far more to "Hispanic nationalism" than European socialism or Marxism–Leninism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995177_385-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995177-385">[385]</a></sup> Historian [Richard Gott](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Gott "Richard Gott") remarked that one of the keys to Castro's success was his ability to use the "twin themes of socialism and nationalism" and keep them "endlessly in play".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGott2004149_386-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGott2004149-386">[386]</a></sup> Castro described Karl Marx and Cuban nationalist José Martí as his main political influences,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009101–102_387-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009101%E2%80%93102-387">[387]</a></sup> although Gott believed that Martí ultimately remained more important than Marx in Castro's politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGott2004149_386-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGott2004149-386">[386]</a></sup> Castro described Martí's political ideas as "a philosophy of independence and an exceptional humanistic philosophy",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009147_388-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009147-388">[388]</a></sup> and his supporters and apologists repeatedly claimed that there were great similarities between the two figures.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELecuona199146_389-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTELecuona199146-389">[389]</a></sup>

Biographer Volker Skierka described Castro's government as a "highly individual, socialist-nationalist '_fidelista_' system",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkierka2006xv_390-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkierka2006xv-390">[390]</a></sup> with Theodore Draper terming his approach "Castroism", viewing it as a blend of European socialism with the Latin American revolutionary tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDraper196548–49_391-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDraper196548%E2%80%9349-391">[391]</a></sup> Political scientist Paul C. Sondrol has described Castro's approach to politics as "totalitarian utopianism",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESondrol1991610_392-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESondrol1991610-392">[392]</a></sup> with a style of leadership that drew upon the wider Latin American phenomenon of the _caudillo_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESondrol1991607,_609_393-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESondrol1991607,_609-393">[393]</a></sup> He drew inspiration from the wider Latin American anti-imperialist movements of the 1930s and 1940s, including Argentina's [Perón](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Per%C3%B3n "Perón") and Guatemala's [Jacobo Árbenz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacobo_%C3%81rbenz "Jacobo Árbenz").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995176_394-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995176-394">[394]</a></sup> Castro took a relatively [socially conservative](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socially_conservative "Socially conservative") stance on many issues, opposing drug use, gambling, and prostitution, which he viewed as [moral evils](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_evil "Moral evil"). Instead, he advocated hard work, family values, integrity, and self-discipline.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986200_395-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986200-395">[395]</a></sup> Although his government repressed [homosexual activity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexual_activity "Homosexual activity") for decades, later in his life he took responsibility for this persecution, regretting it as a "great injustice", as he himself put it.<sup id="cite_ref-396"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-396">[396]</a></sup>

## Personal and public life

### Personality

Juan Reynaldo Sánchez, Castro's former bodyguard, detailed much of his personal and private life in his book _The Double Life of Fidel Castro_. He described Castro as "Nothing ordinary about him at all, he is unique, special, and different."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201560_397-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201560-397">[397]</a></sup> He profiled him as an [egocentric](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egocentric "Egocentric") who loved being the center of attention and, with his almost electric charisma, grabbed the attention of the people around him. He was also highly manipulative; with his formidable intelligence, he could easily manipulate a person or group of people. In addition, he was repetitive and obsessive. In discussions with his colleagues or foreigners, he would repeat the same things repeatedly until they were convinced he was right. It was impossible to contradict him on any subject whatsoever. Anyone who attempted to convince him that he was wrong or even made a suggestion that it could be improved slightly was making a "fatal error." Fidel would then make a mental mark of the individual as an "idiot" and wait for the right time to retaliate against them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez20155_398-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez20155-398">[398]</a></sup> Nobody, not even Raúl was exempt from this; despite being the [minister of the armed forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_(Cuba) "Ministry of the Revolutionary Armed Forces (Cuba)"), he would bring seemingly minor military decisions to Castro for his final approval to avoid inadvertently contradicting him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015192_399-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015192-399">[399]</a></sup> Sánchez believed that General Arnaldo Ochoa's downfall was significantly related to his willingness to contradict Fidel's orders in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201557_400-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201557-400">[400]</a></sup>

Biographer [Leycester Coltman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leycester_Coltman "Leycester Coltman") described Castro as "fiercely hard-working, dedicated, loyal ... generous and magnanimous" but noted that he could be "vindictive and unforgiving." He asserted that Castro "always had a keen sense of humor and could laugh at himself" but could equally be "a bad loser" who would act with "ferocious rage if he thought that he was being humiliated." <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman200314_401-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman200314-401">[401]</a></sup> Publicly, he was known for throwing tantrums and could make "snap judgments," which he refused to back down from.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993494_402-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993494-402">[402]</a></sup> In private, though, Castro was skilled at keeping his anger in check and not allowing it to affect his judgment, simply becoming cold and withdrawn; Sánchez stated that in 17 years, he had only seen Castro explode in anger twice, one upon being informed of his daughter Alina's defection in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201572_403-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201572-403">[403]</a></sup>

Castro was known for working long hours; he primarily woke up late—rarely before ten or eleven in the morning—and started his working day around noon, and would work until late at night, often only going to bed at 3 or 4 am.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003219_404-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003219-404">[404]</a></sup> He preferred to meet foreign diplomats in these early hours, believing that they would be tired and he could gain the upper hand in negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk199311_405-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk199311-405">[405]</a></sup> Castro liked to meet with ordinary citizens, both in Cuba and abroad, but took a particularly paternal attitude toward Cubans, treating them as if "they were a part of his own giant family." <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986273_406-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986273-406">[406]</a></sup> British historian [Alex von Tunzelmann](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_von_Tunzelmann "Alex von Tunzelmann") commented that "though ruthless, \[Castro\] was a patriot, a man with a profound sense that it was his mission to save the Cuban people." Political scientist Paul C. Sondrol characterized Castro as "quintessentially [totalitarian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarianism "Totalitarianism") in his charismatic appeal, utopian functional role and public, transformative utilisation of power."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESondrol1991601_407-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESondrol1991601-407">[407]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Tunzelmann201194_408-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Tunzelmann201194-408">[408]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fidel_castro_angel_1954.jpg)

Castro with his son Ángel in 1954

Balfour described Castro as having a "voracity for knowledge" and "elephantine memory" that allowed him to speak for hours on various subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995180_409-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995180-409">[409]</a></sup> His hero was [Alexander the Great](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great "Alexander the Great"), whose Spanish equivalent _Alejandro_ he adopted as his _nom de guerre_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201574_410-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201574-410">[410]</a></sup> Castro was a voracious reader; amongst his favorite authors were [Ernest Hemingway](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway "Ernest Hemingway"), [Franz Kafka](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franz_Kafka "Franz Kafka"), [William Shakespeare](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare "William Shakespeare"), and [Maxim Gorky](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxim_Gorky "Maxim Gorky"). He named _[For Whom the Bell Tolls](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/For_Whom_the_Bell_Tolls "For Whom the Bell Tolls")_ his favorite book, committing several portions of the novel to memory and using some of its lessons as a guerrilla fighter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986204_411-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986204-411">[411]</a></sup> He enjoyed art and photography and was known as a patron of both within Cuba but was uninterested in music and disliked dancing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003224_292-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003224-292">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201560_397-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201560-397">[397]</a></sup> He was also an avid fan of cinema, particularly Soviet films. His favorite film was the five-hour long 1967 adaption of [Leo Tolstoy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_Tolstoy "Leo Tolstoy")'s _[War and Peace](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_and_Peace_(film_series) "War and Peace (film series)")_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201548_412-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201548-412">[412]</a></sup> Castro had a lifelong passion, almost obsession, with cows and, starting in 1966, with bovine genetics and breeding. State media frequently published details of his attempts to breed cows with increased milk yields.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201544_413-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201544-413">[413]</a></sup> This interest reached its peak in 1982 when a cow that Fidel had bred, "[Ubre Blanca](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ubre_Blanca "Ubre Blanca")", broke the Guinness World Record for producing 29 gallons of milk live on national television. She was promoted into a national celebrity and propaganda tool, and when the cow died in 1985, _Granma_ published an official obituary for her on the front page, and the postal service issued stamps in her honor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201544_413-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201544-413">[413]</a></sup>

[Fidel Castro's religious beliefs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro%27s_religious_beliefs "Fidel Castro's religious beliefs") have been a matter of some debate; he was [baptized](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baptized "Baptized") and raised as a Roman Catholic. He criticized the use of the Bible to justify the oppression of women and Africans,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet200940–41_414-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet200940%E2%80%9341-414">[414]</a></sup> but commented that Christianity exhibited "a group of very humane precepts" which gave the world "ethical values" and a "sense of social justice," relating, "If people call me Christian, not from the standpoint of religion but from the standpoint of social vision, I declare that I am a Christian."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009156_415-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastroRamonet2009156-415">[415]</a></sup> During a visit of American minister and activist [Jesse Jackson](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_Jackson "Jesse Jackson"), Castro accompanied him to a [Methodist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Methodist "Methodist") church service where he even spoke from the pulpit with a Bible before him, an event that marked a beginning of increased openness towards Christianity in Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-416"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-416">[416]</a></sup> He promoted the idea that [Jesus Christ](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus_in_Christianity "Jesus in Christianity") was a communist, citing the [feeding of the 5,000](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeding_the_multitude "Feeding the multitude") and the story of [Jesus and the rich young man](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus_and_the_rich_young_man "Jesus and the rich young man") as evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993695_417-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993695-417">[417]</a></sup>

### Public image

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Castro_sign.jpg)

Cuban propaganda poster proclaiming a quote from Castro: "_Luchar contra lo imposible y vencer_" ("To fight against the impossible and win")

Within Cuba, Castro was primarily referred to by his official military title _Comandante En Jefe_; he was usually addressed as _Comandante_ (The Commander) in general discourse as well as in person but could also be addressed as _El Jefe_ (the Chief) in the third person, particularly within the party and military command.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201511_418-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201511-418">[418]</a></sup> Castro was often nicknamed "_El Caballo_" ("The Horse"), a label attributed to Cuban entertainer [Benny Moré](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benny_Mor%C3%A9 "Benny Moré"), which alludes to Castro's well-known philandering during the 1950s and early 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003219Gott2004175_419-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003219Gott2004175-419">[419]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-420"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-420">[420]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-421"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-421">[421]</a></sup>

With his [logorrheic](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/logorrheic "wikt:logorrheic") oratorical abilities and profound charisma, Castro was highly skilled at manipulation and deception, quickly whipping up his audience and entire population segments into support. Large throngs of supporters gathered to cheer at Castro's fiery speeches, which typically lasted for hours (even outdoors in inclement weather) and without the use of written notes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993312,_688_422-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993312,_688-422">[422]</a></sup> During speeches, Castro regularly cited reports and books he had read on various subjects, including military matters, plant cultivation, filmmaking, and chess strategies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993352–353_423-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993352%E2%80%93353-423">[423]</a></sup> Officially, the Cuban government did maintain a [cult of personality](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cult_of_personality "Cult of personality"). However, unlike other Soviet-era leaders and his allies, it was less widespread and took on a more subtle and discreet form.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015244_424-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015244-424">[424]</a></sup> There were no statues or large portraits of him but rather signs with "thoughts" of the _Comandante_. His popularity among segments of the Cuban populace led to one development without the government's involvement. It would be used to judge each individual's devotion to his "revolutionary cause." <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993255Gott2004325_425-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993255Gott2004325-425">[425]</a></sup> Indeed, by 2006, Castro's image could frequently be found in Cuban stores, classrooms, taxicabs, and on national television.<sup id="cite_ref-426"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-426">[426]</a></sup> In private, however, Castro hated such idolization campaigns and believed that he had intellectual ascendancy over leaders who engaged in such behavior, such as his friend [Kim Il Sung](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Il_Sung "Kim Il Sung") of [North Korea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea") whose cult of personality he considered excessive, outlandish and unreasonable.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015245_427-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015245-427">[427]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fidel_Castro_2012.jpg)

Castro in his characteristic green fatigues, 2012

He gave no importance to his appearance or clothing; for 37 years, he wore only his trademark olive-green military fatigues or the standard [MINFAR](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/MINFAR "MINFAR") dress uniform for formal events and special occasions, emphasizing his role as the perpetual revolutionary, but in the mid-1990s began wearing dark civilian suits and _[guayabera](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guayabera "Guayabera")_ in public.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015303–304_428-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015303%E2%80%93304-428">[428]</a></sup> At over 6 feet 3 inches (1.91 m) tall with a few inches added from his combat boots, Castro usually towered over most foreign leaders he met with, giving him a dominating presence in any room or photo that was taken, which he used to his advantage (for comparison, [Abraham Lincoln](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln "Abraham Lincoln") and [Charles de Gaulle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle "Charles de Gaulle"), both well known for their tall heights, stood at 6'4" and 6'5", respectively). Until his uprising against Batista, Castro typically kept a pencil-thin mustache and combed back hair, typical of upper-class Cuban men in the 1950s, but grew out both during his years as a guerrilla fighter and retained them afterward. Castro also disliked worrying about his appearance and hated shaving, making the beard and uniform all the more convenient for him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201556_429-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201556-429">[429]</a></sup> His uniform was also kept simple; he never wore any medals or decorations, and his only marker of rank was the _Comandante El Jefe_ insignia stitched on the shoulder straps. Until the 1990s, he wore combat boots, but he abandoned them for sneakers and tennis shoes instead due to orthopedic issues. Around his waist, he often carried a 9mm Browning pistol in a brown leather holster with three additional magazines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015105_430-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015105-430">[430]</a></sup> His weapon of choice was a 7.62 Kalashnikov [AKM](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/AKM "AKM"), which Castro occasionally carried with him during the 1960s but was later kept stored in a suitcase carried by one of the members of his escort or kept placed between his feet while driving along with five cartridges; he frequently used it during shooting exercises and practice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015129_431-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015129-431">[431]</a></sup> Castro had a lifelong love of guns and was considered an expert sharpshooter, impressing foreign visitors and even holding up against members of his elite bodyguards who engaged in frequent competition with him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk199310,_255_432-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk199310,_255-432">[432]</a></sup>

Castro's most iconic public feature eventually became the Cuban cigar he smoked daily. Introduced to it by his father at the age of 15, Castro continued the habit for almost 44 years except for a brief period during the 1950s while he was a guerrilla fighter and boycotting against Batista-linked tobacco firms.<sup id="cite_ref-cigaraficionado.com_433-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-cigaraficionado.com-433">[433]</a></sup> Castro claimed that he quit around 1985 during an anti-smoking campaign promoted by the Communist Party. Sánchez disputes this, saying that his doctor had Castro reduce his cigar usage starting in 1980 and quit entirely in 1983 after a cancerous ulcer was found in his intestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015274_434-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015274-434">[434]</a></sup> Prior to the Revolution, Castro smoked various brands including [Romeo y Julieta](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romeo_y_Julieta_(cigar) "Romeo y Julieta (cigar)") Churchill, [H. Upmann](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._Upmann "H. Upmann"), Bauza, and [Partagás](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partag%C3%A1s_(cigar_brand) "Partagás (cigar brand)"). In the early 1960s, Castro saw one of his bodyguards smoking a noticeably aromatic but unbranded cigar. Castro and the bodyguard located the cigar maker, Eduardo Ribera, who agreed to establish the El Laguito Factory and branded the cigars as [Cohiba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cohiba_(cigar_brand) "Cohiba (cigar brand)") which became Castro's signature brand and elevating its profile internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-cigaraficionado.com_433-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-cigaraficionado.com-433">[433]</a></sup> Initially restricted for his private use and other members of the Politburo, it was later presented as diplomatic gifts for allied countries and friends of Castro, most notably seen smoked by [Che Guevara](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara "Che Guevara"), [Josip Broz Tito](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito "Josip Broz Tito"), [Houari Boumédiène](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houari_Boum%C3%A9di%C3%A8ne "Houari Boumédiène"), [Sukarno](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sukarno "Sukarno"), and [Saddam Hussein](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein").<sup id="cite_ref-cigaraficionado.com_433-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-cigaraficionado.com-433">[433]</a></sup>

### Lifestyle

Castro's primary residence was at _Punto Cero_, a large and vegetative estate approximately 6 km from the _Palacio de la Revolution_ in the Siboney neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201579_435-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201579-435">[435]</a></sup> The main house is an L-shaped two-story family mansion with a 600-square-yard footprint, a 50-foot-long swimming pool, six greenhouses providing fruit and vegetables for Fidel's and Raúl's families as well as their bodyguard units, and a large lawn with free-range chickens and cows. Close by is a second two-story building that houses the bodyguards and the domestic staff.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201579_435-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201579-435">[435]</a></sup> The house was decorated in a classical Caribbean style, with local wicker and wood furniture, porcelain plates, watercolor paintings, and art books. Sánchez described the estate as naturally beautiful and tastefully decorated, and while considered luxurious for the average Cuban, was not lavish or over-the-top compared to the residences of the [Somoza clan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somoza_family "Somoza family") or the [Kim dynasty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_family_(North_Korea) "Kim family (North Korea)") of North Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201580_436-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201580-436">[436]</a></sup> Raúl and [Vilma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilma_Esp%C3%ADn "Vilma Espín")'s house _La Rinconada_ is located close by on 222nd street. Raúl usually hosted large family barbecues on Sundays, where Fidel would sometimes come, giving his extended family, sisters, and elder brother Ramón a rare opportunity to see him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015195_437-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015195-437">[437]</a></sup> Next to _Punto Cero_ is _Unit 160_ which was the base of Fidel's bodyguard units. The base was over five acres large and surrounded by high walls, essentially a "city within a city" consisting of support personnel for transportation, communications, electronics, and food, and an extensive armory of Kalashnikovs, Makarovs, and Brownings. Members of that unit also assisted in Fidel's passion for Bovine breeding, and a stable was kept for some of Fidel's most prized cows.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201549_438-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201549-438">[438]</a></sup>

In addition to "Punto Cero," Castro had five other residences in Havana: _Casa Cojimar_, his initial home after 1959 but disused by the 1970s; a house on 160th Street near the Playa district; _Casa Carbonell_, maintained by Cuban Intelligence for his covert meetings with representatives of foreign groups or intelligence assets; A beach house in Santa Maria del Mar (next to the Tropico Hotel); and two houses retrofitted with air-raid shelters and connected to the MINFAR command bunkers for use in war: _Casa Punta Brava_ (Dalia's old house before meeting Fidel) and _Casa Gallego_, near the bodyguards base at Unit 160. In the west of Cuba, he had three residences: _Casa Americana_ (confiscated from an American businessman connected to Batista); _Rancho la Tranquilidad_ in the locality of Mil Cumbres; and La Deseada, a hunting lodge utilized in the winter for duck hunting and fishing trips. He also had two homes in Matanzas, one in Ciego de Avila, a horse ranch _Hacienda San Cayetano_ in Camaguey along with another house in a vacation compound for the Politburo nearby, _Casa Guardalavaca_ in Holguin, and two residences in Santiago de Cuba (One of which is shared with [Ramiro Valdes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramiro_Valdes "Ramiro Valdes")).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015268_439-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015268-439">[439]</a></sup>

Castro's main vacation destination was Cayo de Piedra, a small key island formerly the site of a lighthouse, approximately a mile long and divided into two by a cyclone in the 1960s. He came upon the island by accident while reviewing the region in the aftermath of the failed Bay of Pigs invasion. Instantly falling in love with the island, he ordered it closed off and had the lighthouse demolished.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201514_440-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201514-440">[440]</a></sup> [Osmany Cienfuegos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmany_Cienfuegos "Osmany Cienfuegos") designed the private bungalow, guesthouse, bridge, marina, and a building for the use of the bodyguards and support staff.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201515_441-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201515-441">[441]</a></sup> He arrived from his inaccessible private marina near the Bay of Pigs, _La Caleta del Rosario_, which also housed another residence and guesthouse.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201510_442-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201510-442">[442]</a></sup> Castro used two yachts, _Aquarama I_, confiscated from a Batista Government official and later in the 1970s, the 90-foot white hull _Aquarama II_. _Aquarama II_, which was decorated with wood donated from [Angola](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angola "Angola"), had two double cabins, one for Fidel's personal use, a main sitting room, two bathrooms, a bar, a secure communications suite, and was equipped with four [Osa-class missile boat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osa-class_missile_boat "Osa-class missile boat") engines gifted from Brezhnev allowing for top speeds of over 42 Knots.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez20159_443-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez20159-443">[443]</a></sup> _Aquarama II_ had two companion speedboats used by his escort, _Pioniera I_ and _Pioniera II_; one was equipped with a large cache of weapons, and another was equipped with medical equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez20157_444-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez20157-444">[444]</a></sup>

Castro also had a keen interest in [gastronomy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gastronomy "Gastronomy") and was known to wander into his kitchen to discuss cookery with his chefs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003224_292-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003224-292">[292]</a></sup> His diet was quintessentially Cuban, based on traditional pescatarian cuisine and the additional influence from his native Galicia. All of his food was sourced from Punto Cero or fished from his private island of Cayo Piedra, except for cases of [Algerian Red Wine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_wine "Algerian wine") gifted initially from [Houari Boumediene](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houari_Boumediene "Houari Boumediene") and continued by successive Algerian governments and Iraqi figs and fruit jams from Saddam Hussein.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201584_445-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201584-445">[445]</a></sup> Castro, who typically woke up in the late morning, usually had tea or fish [bouillon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Broth "Broth") for breakfast accompanied by milk provided from one of the cows that grazed on _Punto Cero_; they were all bred to provide milk which suited Castro's demanding taste. His lunches were also frugal, consisting of fish or seafood soup with fresh produce. Dinner was his primary meal, consisting of grilled fish, chicken, mutton, or even _pata negra_ ham on special occasions, along with a large serving of green vegetables. However, he was prevented from eating beef or coffee by his dietician. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201583_446-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201583-446">[446]</a></sup>

Until 1979, Castro's primary vehicle was a black [ZiL](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZiL "ZiL") limousine, first an armored convertible [ZIL-111](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZIL-111 "ZIL-111") from Khrushchev, a [ZIL-114](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZIL-114 "ZIL-114") and briefly a [ZIL-4104](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZIL-4104 "ZIL-4104") gifted to him by Leonid Brezhnev, while his escort would accompany him in several [Alfa Romeo 1750s and 2000s](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_1750_Berlina "Alfa Romeo 1750 Berlina").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015104_447-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015104-447">[447]</a></sup> In 1979, during the Non-Aligned Movement summit at Havana, Saddam Hussein gave Castro his Armored [Mercedes-Benz 560 SEL](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_W126 "Mercedes-Benz W126"), which he had brought from Baghdad and became his sole transport for the rest of his life. Subsequently, Fidel ordered two mechanics from his bodyguard unit to West Germany to purchase several second-hand Mercedes-Benz 500s to replace the obsolete Alfa Romeos.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015104_447-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015104-447">[447]</a></sup> Castro always traveled with at least fourteen guards and four of his aides, spread out over four vehicles: three Mercedes-Benz and one Soviet Lada, which trailed the main convoy (to keep the military presence at a minimal). Whenever he would leave Havana, a fifth Mercedes would join the procession carrying his doctor, nurse, and photographer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015100_448-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015100-448">[448]</a></sup>

The "[Forbes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")" magazine ranked Castro as the 7th wealthiest ruler in the world at an estimated personal wealth of approximately 900 million US dollars in 2006 (going from 550 million US dollars in their 2005 list). The estimate is based on the magazine's assumption that Castro had economic control over a network of state-owned companies, including [CIMEX](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIMEX "CIMEX"), Medicuba, the Havana Convention Palace, and the assumption that a portion of their profits went to Castro through investments.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera-2006_449-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-aljazeera-2006-449">[449]</a></sup> Suggesting that Castro's fortune multiplied, growing from 103 million to 850 million euros (equivalent to 900 million dollars) in just three years,<sup id="cite_ref-informeorwell-2023_450-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-informeorwell-2023-450">[450]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-infobae-2016_451-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-infobae-2016-451">[451]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-clarin-2016_452-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-clarin-2016-452">[452]</a></sup> the "Forbes" article also referred to rumours of Castro's [Swiss bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banking_in_Switzerland "Banking in Switzerland") accounts with "large stashes" of this fortune.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera-2006_449-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-aljazeera-2006-449">[449]</a></sup> According to Juan Reinaldo Sánchez, a former personal bodyguard of Castro, his assets included Cayo Piedra, a private island; over twenty mansions; a marina with yachts; encrypted bank accounts; and a gold mine.<sup id="cite_ref-informeorwell-2023_450-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-informeorwell-2023-450">[450]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-infobae-2016_451-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-infobae-2016-451">[451]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-clarin-2016_452-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-clarin-2016-452">[452]</a></sup>

### Relationships

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Barbudos_-_Fidel_Castro_and_Camilo_Cienfuegos.jpg)

Castro and [Camilo Cienfuegos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camilo_Cienfuegos "Camilo Cienfuegos") before playing a baseball game

In his personal life, Castro was known for being distant, withdrawn, and confided in very few people. His closest and most trusted friend was Raúl Castro, his younger brother by five years and longtime armed forces minister.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201541_453-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201541-453">[453]</a></sup> Although Raúl had a vastly contrasting, almost polar opposite personality to Castro, Sánchez described Raúl as complementing Castro's personality in all the ways that he is not. Whereas Fidel was "charismatic, energetic, visionary but extremely impulsive and disorganized," Raúl was described as a "natural, methodical, and uncompromising organizer." Castro spoke nearly daily with Raúl, met several times a week, and was a frequent visitor at Raúl and Vilma's house; Vilma was also considered close to Castro and often appeared publicly with him at national events.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015188_454-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015188-454">[454]</a></sup> Besides Raúl, Castro was not close to any of his other siblings, although he did have friendly relations with his elder brother Ramón and sister Angelita.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015187_455-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015187-455">[455]</a></sup> His sister [Juanita Castro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juanita_Castro "Juanita Castro") had been living in the United States since the early 1960s until her death in 2023 and was a public opponent of the Cuban regime.<sup id="cite_ref-456"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-456">[456]</a></sup>

Outside his immediate family, Castro's closest friend was fellow revolutionary Celia Sánchez, who accompanied him everywhere during the 1960s and controlled almost all access to the leader.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986200–201_457-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986200%E2%80%93201-457">[457]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201541_453-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201541-453">[453]</a></sup> Reynaldo Sánchez confirmed that Celia was indeed Castro's mistress and regarded her as the "true love of his life." <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201541_453-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201541-453">[453]</a></sup> Castro provided a large apartment for Celia on 11th Street near Vedado, _El Once_ whom Fidel visited every day before returning home. Over the years, Castro added an elevator, fitness room, and a bowling alley for his and Celia's personal use. He even provided bodyguards from his escort to Celia for her protection.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201542_458-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201542-458">[458]</a></sup>

Castro's closest male friends were the members of his immediate bodyguard unit, _Escolta_ or the "Escort."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201592_459-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201592-459">[459]</a></sup> His security was provided by Department 1 of the Personal Security Directorate of [MININT](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/MININT "MININT") (Ministry of the Interior). Department 1 was for Fidel's security, Department 2 was for Raúl and Vilma's, and Department 3 was for the members of the Politburo and so on.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201540_460-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201540-460">[460]</a></sup> Unlike the other MININT Departments, his and Raúl's units bypassed the standard chain of command and reported to them directly. Castro's security consisted of three concentric _anillos_ or rings. The third ring consisted of thousands of soldiers in MININT and MINFAR who supported Logistics, air defense, Intelligence, etc.; The second ring consisted of eighty to one hundred soldiers who provided the outer perimeter security; And the first ring, the Elite _Escolta_ or "The Escort," provided his immediate security and consisted of two teams of 15 elite soldiers who worked 24-hour shifts, along with around ten support staff.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201540_460-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201540-460">[460]</a></sup>

A soldier at heart, Castro had more affinity with his escort than his civilian family. He spent most of his time under their protection and were usually his companions in his personal interests.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201592_459-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201592-459">[459]</a></sup> A sports fan, he also spent much of his time trying to keep fit, undertaking regular exercise such as hunting, fly fishing, underwater fishing, scuba diving, and playing basketball.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201593_461-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201593-461">[461]</a></sup> They were also his companions on special events, such as his birthday or national holidays, during which they regularly exchanged gifts and engaged in one-sided discussions with Castro where he would recall his life stories. The members of Escort Castro were closest to the former Mayor of Havana, Jose "Pepín" Naranjo, who became his official aide until he died in 1995, and his physician, Eugenio Selman. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201511_418-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201511-418">[418]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986201_462-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986201-462">[462]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-463"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-463">[463]</a></sup> Outside of his escort, Castro was also close to [Manuel "Barbarroja" Pineiro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Pi%C3%B1eiro "Manuel Piñeiro"), the head of the American Department of the [DGI](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direcci%C3%B3n_de_Inteligencia "Dirección de Inteligencia"), [Antonio Núñez Jiménez](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonio_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_Jim%C3%A9nez "Antonio Núñez Jiménez"), and the Colombian novelist [Gabriel García Márquez](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez "Gabriel García Márquez").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986299_464-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986299-464">[464]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201594_465-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201594-465">[465]</a></sup>

### Marital history

The Cuban Government has never published an official marital history of Castro, with most information coming from defectors and scarce details published in state media and pieced together over the years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkierka20063_466-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkierka20063-466">[466]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-467"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-467">[467]</a></sup> In his earlier years in power, he showcased some of his family life, in particular his eldest son Fidelito to portray himself as a regular "family man" to the apprehensive American audience, but eventually abandoned that as he became more concerned about his safety.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201565_468-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201565-468">[468]</a></sup> Throughout his rule, Castro never named an official "First Lady" and when the need for such a public female companion was necessary, Celia Sánchez or Raúl's wife, Vilma Espín, would play such a role of _la primera dama_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201562_469-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201562-469">[469]</a></sup>

Sánchez described Castro as a compulsive lover or "womanizer"; he has been officially married twice but has carried on numerous affairs, including many one-night stands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201560_397-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201560-397">[397]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993231_470-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993231-470">[470]</a></sup> Popular with women and often recognized as a [sex symbol](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_symbol "Sex symbol") in Cuba,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986201_462-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986201-462">[462]</a></sup> Castro never had difficulty in finding love and seduction. Sánchez denies that Castro ever engaged in any unusual or un-consensual behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201560_397-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201560-397">[397]</a></sup> Castro was also described as a poor father; often absent from their lives, he had little interest in his children's activities and was more interested in his work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201563_471-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201563-471">[471]</a></sup> Raúl, who had much stronger paternal feelings towards his family, was often the one who played the role of surrogate father to Castro's children, in particular Fidelito and Alina.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015194_472-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015194-472">[472]</a></sup>

-   Castro's first wife was [Mirta Díaz-Balart](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirta_D%C3%ADaz-Balart "Mirta Díaz-Balart"), whom he married in October 1948. She is the only spouse of Castro acknowledged by the Cuban Government. Diaz-Balart, the daughter of a powerful Cuban politician and brother of Batista's Minister of Interior, was a student at the University of Havana, where she met and married Castro. She divorced him later, in 1955, while he was in prison due to the attacks on the Moncada Barracks. They had one son:
    -   [Fidel Ángel "Fidelito" Castro Díaz-Balart](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro_D%C3%ADaz-Balart "Fidel Castro Díaz-Balart"), born in September 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBardach200767_473-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBardach200767-473">[473]</a></sup> Fidelito grew up at various times between Havana and Miami; he later went to the Soviet Union to study [Nuclear Physics](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_Physics "Nuclear Physics"). For a time, he ran Cuba's atomic-energy commission before being removed from the post by his father.<sup id="cite_ref-anderson_474-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-anderson-474">[474]</a></sup> He took his own life in February 2018, over a year after his father's death.<sup id="cite_ref-475"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-475">[475]</a></sup>
-   During his first marriage, Castro briefly encountered Maria Laborde, an admirer from Camaguey, whom very little is known and has long been deceased. They had one son:
    -   Jorge Ángel Castro was born on 23 March 1949. It was long believed that his birth was in 1956, but Sánchez and another defector uncovered that he was in fact born earlier than Fidelito.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201568_476-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201568-476">[476]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hart_477-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Hart-477">[477]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-478"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-478">[478]</a></sup>
-   While Castro was married to Mirta, he had an affair with [Natalia "Naty" Revuelta Clews](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalia_Revuelta_Clews "Natalia Revuelta Clews"). Widely regarded in Havana for her beauty, Natalia was married to Dr. Orlando Fernandez but sympathized with the aims of the Revolutionary movement. She initially joined the movement as a friend of Castro but later became his mistress and visited him while imprisoned in Isla de Pinos.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201569_479-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201569-479">[479]</a></sup> She would give birth to his daughter:
    -   [Alina Fernández Revuelta](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alina_Fern%C3%A1ndez "Alina Fernández"),<sup id="cite_ref-anderson_474-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-anderson-474">[474]</a></sup> born in 1956, is Castro's only daughter. She did not know her true parentage until she was 10. Castro showed little interest in her but sent her to a boarding school in Saint-Germain-en-Laye, France. One of the few people willing to stand up to Castro, several defectors have described her personality as the most similar to her father.
