Alina became a public relations director for a State-owned fashion company and a model for [Havana Club](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Havana_Club "Havana Club"). Her father inadvertently found out about the latter job while reading _Cuba_ magazine, coming across an advertisement showing Alina posing in a bikini on a boat with two other models; he nearly exploded with rage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201570_480-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201570-480">[480]</a></sup> Alina left Cuba in 1993, disguised as a Spanish tourist,<sup id="cite_ref-481"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-481">[481]</a></sup> and sought asylum in the US, from where she has criticized her father's policies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández1997_482-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFern%C3%A1ndez1997-482">[482]</a></sup>
-   Castro's second and longest wife was with Dalia Soto Del Valle, another admirer who met Castro during a speech in Villa Clara in 1961. She was a teacher who was part of the Government's literacy campaign. She moved to Havana on Castro's initiative and later moved in with him at _Punto Cero_ as his permanent family. Her relationship with Castro was kept secret until 2006 when she was photographed with an increasingly frail Castro during the Party Congress, although the Cuban Government has released no other information.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201573_483-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201573-483">[483]</a></sup> Castro and Dalia had five sons, each of them starting with the letter A and three of them a variation of "Alexander" (in homage to Alexander the Great, his pseudonym while a guerrilla fighter):<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201574_410-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201574-410">[410]</a></sup>
    -   Alexis Castro Del Valle, born in 1962. Described as a loner with few friends, he eventually got a degree in computer science but has since become a mechanic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201575_484-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201575-484">[484]</a></sup>
    -   Alex Castro Del Valle, born in 1963. Much more affable and outgoing, he was initially trained as an engineer as well but instead became a photographer and cameraman for _[Granma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Granma_(newspaper) "Granma (newspaper)")_ and [Cubavisión](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cubavisi%C3%B3n "Cubavisión"), respectively. He later became the official photographer of his father and, published several books, and hosted the exhibition _Fidel Castro: Photografia Intimidade_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201576_485-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201576-485">[485]</a></sup>
    -   Alejandro Castro Del Valle, born in 1969. Considered a "computer geek" like his brothers, he also studied computer science and engineering but was passionate about the subject. Around 1990, he wrote software that allowed Russian programs to be run on Japanese ones; the product was purchased by [NEC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/NEC "NEC") of Japan, which raised his national profile in the engineering community of Cuba and even public praise from his father.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201576_485-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201576-485">[485]</a></sup>
    -   Antonio Castro Del Valle, born in 1971. A national youth baseball champion, he studied sports medicine at the University of Havana and became an [Orthopedic surgeon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthopedic_surgeon "Orthopedic surgeon"). He is currently the head of the Surgery unit at the Elite Frank Pais Orthopedic Hospital, a Doctor to the National Baseball team, and President of the Cuban Baseball Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201578_486-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201578-486">[486]</a></sup>
    -   Angelito Castro Del Valle, born in 1974. Considered spoiled by his parents from a young age, he was long considered the "trouble child" of the family. He was passionate about cars and frequently earned the ire of his father's escort unit for disrupting the mechanics' work. Angelito never obtained any higher education but later became the senior executive of the Mercedes-Benz concession of Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez201579_435-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez201579-435">[435]</a></sup>
-   After the 1970s, Castro began a long relationship with Juanita Vera, a Colonel in the foreign intelligence service who joined his escort unit as his English interpreter. She often appeared in public with Castro, in particular in Oliver Stone's _[Comandante](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comandante_(2003_film) "Comandante (2003 film)")_ as his translator and interpreter. She and Castro had one son, Abel Castro Vera, born in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez2015269_487-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTES%C3%A1nchez2015269-487">[487]</a></sup>

Castro had another daughter, Francisca Pupo (born 1953), the result of a one-night affair. Pupo and her husband now live in Miami.<sup id="cite_ref-canf.org_488-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-canf.org-488">[488]</a></sup> Another son known as Ciro was also born in the early 1960s, the result of another brief fling, his existence confirmed by Celia Sánchez.<sup id="cite_ref-Hart_477-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Hart-477">[477]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Family_Tree_of_Fidel_Castro.svg)

Castro's family tree

## Reception and legacy

> Within Cuba, Fidel's domination of every aspect of the government and the society remains total. His personal needs for absolute control seems to have changed little over the years. He remains committed to a disciplined society in which he is still determined to remake the Cuban national character, creating work-orientated, socially concerned individuals ... He wants to increase people's standard of living, the availability of material goods, and to import the latest technology. But the economic realities, despite rapid dramatic growth in the gross national product, severely limit what Cuba can buy on the world market.

– Peter Bourne, Castro biographer, 1986<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986302_489-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986302-489">[489]</a></sup>

One of the most controversial political leaders of his era,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour19951_490-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour19951-490">[490]</a></sup> Castro both inspired and dismayed people around the world during his lifetime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995vi_491-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995vi-491">[491]</a></sup> The London _[Observer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Observer "The Observer")_ stated that he proved to be "as divisive in death as he was in life", and that the only thing that his "enemies and admirers" agreed upon was that he was "a towering figure" who "transformed a small Caribbean island into a major force in world affairs".<sup id="cite_ref-492"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-492">[492]</a></sup> _[The Daily Telegraph](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph "The Daily Telegraph")_ noted that around the world he was "either praised as a brave champion of the people, or derided as a power-mad dictator."<sup id="cite_ref-493"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-493">[493]</a></sup>

According to political scientists, Castro ruled a single-party [authoritarian regime](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_regime "Authoritarian regime") in Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-494"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-494">[494]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-495"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-495">[495]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-496"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-496">[496]</a></sup> Political opposition was not permitted.<sup id="cite_ref-497"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-497">[497]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-498"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-498">[498]</a></sup> According to political scientists Steven Levitsky and Lucan Way, the Cuban regime entailed "full authoritarianism ... (like China and Saudi Arabia)", as there were "no viable channels... for opposition to contest legally for executive power."<sup id="cite_ref-499"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-499">[499]</a></sup> Censorship of information was extensive,<sup id="cite_ref-HRW-Cuba-III-1999_500-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-HRW-Cuba-III-1999-500">[500]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Michael_C._Moynihan_501-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Michael_C._Moynihan-501">[501]</a></sup> and independent journalism was repressed.<sup id="cite_ref-502"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-502">[502]</a></sup>

Despite its small size and limited economic weight, Castro's Cuba gained a large role in world affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour19952_503-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour19952-503">[503]</a></sup> The Castro government relied heavily on its appeals to nationalistic sentiment, in particular the widespread hostility to the US government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995ix_504-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995ix-504">[504]</a></sup> According to Balfour, Castro's domestic popularity stemmed from the fact that he symbolized "a long-cherished hope of national liberation and social justice" for much of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour19953_505-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour19953-505">[505]</a></sup> Balfour also noted that throughout Latin America, Castro served as "a symbol of defiance against the continued economic and [cultural imperialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_imperialism "Cultural imperialism") of the United States".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995170_506-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995170-506">[506]</a></sup> Similarly, [Wayne S. Smith](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Smith_(diplomat) "Wayne Smith (diplomat)")—the former Chief of the [United States Interests Section in Havana](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Interests_Section_in_Havana "United States Interests Section in Havana")—noted that Castro's opposition to US dominance and transformation of Cuba into a significant world player resulted in him receiving "warm applause" throughout the [Western Hemisphere](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Hemisphere "Western Hemisphere").<sup id="cite_ref-Wayne_Smith_507-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-Wayne_Smith-507">[507]</a></sup>

Various Western governments and human rights organizations nevertheless heavily criticized Castro and he was widely reviled in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003290_508-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003290-508">[508]</a></sup> Following Castro's death, US [president-elect](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/President-elect_of_the_United_States "President-elect of the United States") [Donald Trump](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump") called him a "brutal dictator",<sup id="cite_ref-509"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-509">[509]</a></sup> while the Cuban-American politician [Marco Rubio](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Rubio "Marco Rubio") called him "an evil, murderous dictator" who turned Cuba into "an impoverished island prison".<sup id="cite_ref-510"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-510">[510]</a></sup> Castro publicly rejected the "dictator" label, stating that he constitutionally held less power than most heads of state and insisting that his regime allowed for greater democratic involvement in policy making than Western liberal democracies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993529Coltman2003292_511-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993529Coltman2003292-511">[511]</a></sup> Nevertheless, critics claim that Castro wielded significant unofficial influence aside from his official duties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColtman2003292_512-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColtman2003292-512">[512]</a></sup> Quirk stated that Castro wielded "absolute power" in Cuba, albeit not in a legal or constitutional manner,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993501_513-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993501-513">[513]</a></sup> while Bourne claimed that power in Cuba was "completely invested" in Castro,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986263_514-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986263-514">[514]</a></sup> adding that it was very rare for "a country and a people" to have been so completely dominated by "the personality of one man".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986295_515-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986295-515">[515]</a></sup> Balfour stated that Castro's "moral and political hegemony" within Cuba diminished the opportunities for democratic debate and decision making.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995181_516-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour1995181-516">[516]</a></sup> Describing Castro as a "totalitarian dictator",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESondrol1991606_517-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESondrol1991606-517">[517]</a></sup> Sondrol suggested that in leading "a political system largely \[of\] his own creation and bearing his indelible stamp", Castro's leadership style warranted comparisons with totalitarian leaders like [Mao Zedong](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong"), [Hideki Tojo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hideki_Tojo "Hideki Tojo"), [Joseph Stalin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), [Adolf Hitler](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler"), and [Benito Mussolini](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESondrol1991619_518-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESondrol1991619-518">[518]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ben_Bella_a_la_Havane_-_Cuba.jpg)

Castro with [Ahmed Ben Bella](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Ben_Bella "Ahmed Ben Bella"), principal leader of the [Algerian War of Independence](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_War "Algerian War") against French colonial rule; Ben Bella was one of many political figures inspired by Castro<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993424_519-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993424-519">[519]</a></sup>

Noting that there were "few more polarising political figures" than Castro, [Amnesty International](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International") described him as "a progressive but deeply flawed leader". In their view, he should be "applauded" for his regime's "substantial improvements" to healthcare and education, but criticized for its "ruthless suppression of freedom of expression."<sup id="cite_ref-520"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-520">[520]</a></sup> [Human Rights Watch](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch "Human Rights Watch") stated that his government constructed a "repressive machinery" which deprived Cubans of their "basic rights".<sup id="cite_ref-HRW-Castro_521-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-HRW-Castro-521">[521]</a></sup> Castro defended his government's record on human rights, stating that the state was forced to limit the freedoms of individuals and imprison those involved in counter-revolutionary activities to protect the rights of the collective populace, such as the right to employment, education, and health care.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993758Coltman2003247_522-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993758Coltman2003247-522">[522]</a></sup>

Historian and journalist Richard Gott considered Castro to be "one of the most extraordinary political figures of the twentieth century", commenting that he had become a "world hero in the mould" of [Giuseppe Garibaldi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi "Giuseppe Garibaldi") to people throughout the developing world for his anti-imperialist efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGott2004148_523-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGott2004148-523">[523]</a></sup> Balfour stated that Castro's story had "few parallels in contemporary history", for there existed no other "Third World \[_[sic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sic "Sic")_\] leader" in the second half of the twentieth century who held "such a prominent and restless part on the international stage" or remained head of state for such a long period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour19951_490-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour19951-490">[490]</a></sup> Bourne described Castro as "an influential world leader" who commanded "great respect" from individuals of all political ideologies across the developing world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourne1986302_489-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourne1986302-489">[489]</a></sup> Canadian prime minister [Justin Trudeau](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justin_Trudeau "Justin Trudeau") described Castro as a "remarkable leader" and a "larger than life leader who served his people."<sup id="cite_ref-524"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-524">[524]</a></sup> The [European Commission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission") president [Jean-Claude Juncker](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker "Jean-Claude Juncker") said that Castro "was a hero for many."<sup id="cite_ref-525"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-525">[525]</a></sup> Russian president [Vladimir Putin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin") described Castro as both "a sincere and reliable friend of Russia" and a "symbol of an era", while Chinese Communist Party [general secretary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party "General Secretary of the Chinese Communist Party") [Xi Jinping](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xi_Jinping "Xi Jinping") similarly referred to him as "a close comrade and a sincere friend" to China.<sup id="cite_ref-AlJaz_526-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-AlJaz-526">[526]</a></sup> Indian prime minister [Narendra Modi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi "Narendra Modi") termed him "one of the most iconic personalities of the 20th century" and a "great friend", while South African president [Jacob Zuma](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Zuma "Jacob Zuma") praised Castro for aiding black South Africans in "our struggle against apartheid".<sup id="cite_ref-AlJaz_526-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-AlJaz-526">[526]</a></sup> He was awarded a [wide variety of awards and honours from foreign governments](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_awards_and_honours_bestowed_upon_Fidel_Castro "List of awards and honours bestowed upon Fidel Castro") and was cited as an inspiration for foreign leaders like Ahmed Ben Bella<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993424_519-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuirk1993424-519">[519]</a></sup> and Nelson Mandela,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESampson1999192_527-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESampson1999192-527">[527]</a></sup> who subsequently awarded him South Africa's highest civilian award for foreigners, the [Order of Good Hope](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Good_Hope "Order of Good Hope").<sup id="cite_ref-528"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-528">[528]</a></sup> The biographer Volker Skierka stated that "he will go down in history as one of the few revolutionaries who remained true to his principles".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkierka2006xxiv_529-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkierka2006xxiv-529">[529]</a></sup>
